<Author>HonestEssex_England
<Content>busy, busy, busy Just got back after staying at this hotel Dec 08 and for the new year. What can I say, Hawaii is extremly busy. Not what I quite expected. We arrived on 26th December and after a 9 hour delay on our flight from Las Vegas everything was in complete darkness. Apparently there had been a power cut and the whole of the island had no electricity. As we drove along the streets all we could see were police cars and flares lighting up the streets. You can imagine after the bright lights of Vegas to darkness we were very sceptical. Check in was a breeze, however, we were just told that that there was a flash light in our room so we could see. After 2 visits back to reception we eventually found the flash light, but a match would of given off more light so we just went to bed. The hotel is extremly clean and tidy and the rooms are more a 3+ star than a 5 star. The beach and pool areas are extremly busy and it is very hard to find a spot to sun bathe (this could of been the time of year that we went, but I do like a bit of privacy and not have my next door neighbours sitting on top of me. If you are a smoker this Island may not suit you as you can only smoke in designated areas and smoking is not allowed in the hotel premises at all (not even on your balcony, around th pool, on the beach or walking along the street). However, I must say that we meet some great friends at these smoking stations. The sun loungers around the pool are free , however few and far between. Most of them are reserved for guests that have been staying there for 21 days or more. Drinks are very expenses at the hotel, but we found an ABC store opposite the hotel and brought cans to take to the pool with us. Nobody said anything and everyone seemed to be doing the same. If you sun bathe on the beach you are not allowed to drink alcohol and there are police walking the beat to ensure that this law is enforced. The food is reasonable and I would recommend the buffett breakfast and lunch as food is very plentiful and very nice. There is not much to do in the evenings here unless you like designer shopping as it is very hard to get served in the hotel bar as it is so busy. Even the Americans were calling this New York on the beach. This Island was not what we expected as we thought it would be quieter so we wont be returing to Hawaii.

<Author>J_CVancouver
<Content>Wonderful EXCEPT for the noise.... A lovely hotel, GREAT staff, terrific restaurants, and what a location! BUT, if you want to sleep on your vacation...this property is not a good choice. Walls are paper-thin between rooms and you can hear EVERYTHING going on in the adjoining rooms (on either side, and above). After reporting concerns to the front desk they said we had to call them as soon as we heard the noises (which were more or less non-stop) and they would send Security to investigate...not really something we want to become involved/engaged in during our vacation. People in other rooms were not being that unreasonable...the hotel just needs to do something about soundproofing. There was also a gaggle of musicians making noise for donations directly in front of the International Marketplace (right across the road from this hotel). The drum, electric guitar and steel drum solos carried on until after 2:00 am, making it impossible to have a window open. We spoke with hotel security staff at the entrance and they said there was not really anything they could do about it. It was obvious that we were not the only ones being bothered as we witnessed others voicing similar complaints. I would think the surrounding hotels would be taking steps with the local authorities to establish some guidelines. We spoke with the police at the Waikiki Beach detachment and they had received similar complaints that same day. We live in the heart of downtown Vancouver in a condo and are not unreasonable about city noises, but between the poor sound proofing and the unregulated noise makers across the road we did not get one night of sleep in two weeks! So, if you are hoping to get any rest during your stay in Waikiki I would personally not recommend this otherwise lovely property.

<Author>chookas
<Content>Great location but............ Recently returned from a 5 night stay at Outrigger Waikiki (end of October), staying in an Ocean Front room. The hotel itself is pleasant, the rooms are dated but very clean and spacious. The hotel staff are very friendly and helpful, 10 out of 10 for them. Our only gripe is the construction noise from the hotel directly next to the Outrigger. Of course this isn't the fault of the hotel, but it would have been considerate to perhaps inform us of this when we made our booking. The ocean front rooms aren't cheap, and if we had known about the noise we would have opted for a room on the opposite side of the building or another Outrigger. The construction starts at 7.30/8.00am each morning (including Saturday) and finishes around 5pm. If you like to sleep in or be able to listen to the ocean waves on your balcony this hotel probably isn't for you until the Royal Hawaiin is complete. The pool is also right next to the construction activity, so we spent our days at the beach instead.I'm not trying to bag out this hotel as we enjoyed our stay nevertheless, but if you are going to book contact them and ask if you need to consider where your room is located.

<Author>Sequin-Sue
<Content>A great hotel - right on the beach We are a couple in our twenties who stayed at the Outrigger for a week in May/June 2008. We were deciding for ages between this hotel and the Moana Surfrider, and in the end chose this one for the balcony, as a balcony room was a lot more expensive at the Surfrider. The other hotel on the beach, the Royal Hawaiian, was closing for refurbishment at the time, so that one was never in the equation.The hotel's location is excellent - right on the famous Waikiki Beach, with all the shops, bars and restaurants right on its doorstep. We had a side ocean view room with a balcony. The room was a really good size - it had two double beds in - although the balcony was too small; the ones directly on the front looked much bigger. It was fantastic to wake up to a view of the ocean every morning. The decor was a bit dated in the room and throughout the hotel, but completely acceptable.The pool area isn't that big considering the size of the hotel, although we never had any trouble getting a sun-lounger. There are no parasols though which makes sunbathing in the midday sun almost impossible, unless you are a hard-core bather. There are parasols and beds for hire on the beach, but it was about $40 for two beds and a parasol for the day, which is expensive to do more than once. The beach area does get busy, but its not unbearable.We had breakfast at the hotel pretty much every morning - there's plenty of choice in the buffet. We ate at the hotel in the evening a couple of times too which was very nice and a lovely beach-front setting. We would also recommend the restaurant 'Top of Waikiki' - which is the revolving restaurant that can be seen from the main street, it gives excellent views of Honolulu especially at sunset.I think if we went back to Waikiki again we would choose one of the other hotels along the front, but I would certainly recommend the Outrigger for a pleasant stay,

Unless you're a very heavy sleeper this may cause you problems. If I return to Waikiki I think I'd try another hotel just because we had trouble sleeping here.

<Author>Ca_natives
<Content>A Great Week at the Outrigger l We spent a lovely 6 nights  days at the Outrigger in Waikiki. Our room was a little dated (no heavenly bed, but it was comfortable) with a partial ocean view on the 16th floor. This hotel is right in the center of the Waikiki beach. In the front you have shops  restaurants galore. In the back you have beautiful Waikiki. Plus the Outrigger has two of our favorite restaurants (Dukes  Hula Grill). We stay more often in Maui  also love Kimo's, Hula Grill  Leilani's, all in the same family as well as Sunnyside in Lake Tahoe (the family of restaurants used to include Jakes on the Lake in Tahoe). There is so much to do staying at the Outrigger! You can dine, shop, sunbathe, people watch, surfer watch, swim, float, go for a boat ride or a sunset cruise. At night most of the restaurants have entertainment, great local musicians! You can listen to music in the late afternoon at Dukes, go to the Hula Grill and listen to the music there, when that set is through head over to the Sheraton Surfrider and listen to music under the stars and the beautiful banyan tree, then end the night listening to the musicians at Dukes . They have good entertainment at the Hilton, also! Take a trip to Kailua and enjoy the beautiful beach and go kayaking. Meander up to the North Shore  watch the surfers. We had a great time! Next year we're looking at 2 weeks in Maui, but maybe we can take some of that time and come back to Waikiki!

<Author>HappyTraveller7503
<Content>Loved the Outrigger!!! I was a little worried about some of the reviews that the Outrigger had received before I stayed there. Comments about their thin walls, outdated furnishings and the dreaded fans from the Cheesecake Factory were posted many times. However, I couldn't have been more relieved when I got there and experienced this hotel first hand.From the time we arrived, we were greeted promptly and cheerfully. Our check in was a breeze even though we arrived well before check in time. We took possession of one room while we waited for the other to become available.The rooms were a decent size, very comfortably furnished and had plenty of room for two friends and a toddler. My room was above the Cheesecake Factory but because we had the door shut all the time, we didn't hear a thing. We were also on the 9th floor which probably helped!! Our other friends had a room across the hall which had views of the ocean and they had their lanai door open all the time and could only hear the waves coming in - except when the Aloha Parade went through the first weekend we were there.We ate at every restaurant and had breakfast at the Hula Grill every morning. All the waitstaff were incredibly friendly and helpful and often helped us with suggestions of where to go and what to do.The pool is lovely - it's in full shade every morning and although it's really deep even at the shallow end, it is busy all the time so get there early and secure your sun-lounge!The beach outside is pristine and warm and it's easy to find your own little pozzie and share some shade from someone else's sun umbrella! There is a lot to do just on the beach itself - surfiing, canoeing, catamaran-ing.Outrigger on the Beach is in a fantastic location - right in the middle of everything. We used the valet parking and were very happy with the service of the guys there. Also, having computer and ATM access right in our lobby made things that little bit more convenient. As did having a coin laundry to wash baby clothes.We were all thrilled with the Outrigger on the Beach, I don't know if were were more tolerant of our neighbours because we have all travelled extensively and we have a realistic expectation of what a hotel in the middle of the main street in Waikiki is going to be able to deliver, but regardless, none of us had any problems with noisy neighbours or loud flushing toilets and I am already planning to go back and stay again!

<Author>One+Two
<Content>Great for a KB (kick-back) Hawaiian Trip! My family and I stayed here for ten days in early August 2008. The Outrigger has a lot of things going for it. First of all, I found all of the staff very friendly, from the check-in to the restaurants, shops, UPS store (forgot my wallet after I'd made copies and they were happy to wait for me to go get it, guess they didn't have a choice, but they were still very nice about it), the deli, and the pool towel guys. Oh, and the valets, very nice guys asking if you need directions, etc. The location is also awesome. If you are thinking about saving money here or off the beach, you can't beat this location. Splurge on the umbrella set-up. There are different choices and you get a discount as guest. There are also canoe rides and outrigger boats running all day. Don't know the prices but everyone seemed to be having a great time. The pool was fun and warm (just the way I like it!). It is quite deep so if you have very young children make sure they have floats. It starts at 3 feet, jumps to 4, then 8. There is also a nice-sized hot tub. I did not order drinks at the pool but there seemed to be plenty of servers so it didn't look like people were waiting long. I also found the food at the restaurants to be very good. The banana/macadamia nut pancakes are great! Also, try the famous hula pie. I did not eat at Chuck's steakhouse, but my mother did and said it was very good. Prices are not cheap, but compared to many Hawaiian resorts, they will not require a second mortgage! I found them rather reasonable. The only complaint I'd have is the drinks were a little weak. Our room was a partial ocean view. It was clean and the closet space was great, one was more like a walk-in and the other was the typical sliding door. It had a sort of tub-shower, which was a small square tub or you could shower. Great for the kids. There was lots of counter space as well. The balcony was angled and small, though. Difficult to move around. As far as noise, you do hear flushing toilets, etc. but I've heard that in even nicer places so don't know how preventable it is. Overall, the hotel is fun and laid-back. I personally prefer more upscale when I travel, but sometimes a place like this can be just right, esp. if you don't want to be nickel and dimed by a 'high-end' resort. Oh, two other things that deserve mention, the hotel allows free long distance to anywhere in the US. I've never seen that before in a hotel. Also, when you order room service, the bill states 'tip already included'. Now how many hotels can say have the integrity to do that? Aloha, and happy travels.

<Author>Sunee
<Content>Walk out the door  My husband and I just returned from a week at the Outrigger Waikiki on the Beach. It's a beautiful hotel right in the heart of the action on Waikiki Beach. The best part about this hotel is the beautiful beach right outside the back door. The beach is clean, with nice soft sand. It's very crowded, so if you like exclusivity, Waikiki may not be for you, as it is a very busy, bustling place with lots of families and people. You can rent two lounge chairs and an umbrella on the beach for $40 a day, but try to get there by 8:00 a.m. since they can sell out. You can then come and go for the day. The pool area lounges (no umbrellas) are free, and they seem to fill up quickly, too. Or you can go to the store (several are within walking distance) and buy your own chairs and umbrella. You don't really need a car since there is plenty to do within walking distance of the hotel, or they can arrange activities for you. If you do rent a car, it's $25 a night for valet parking. Maybe the best thing about this hotel is that--if you fly Hawaiian Airlines--they'll pick up your luggage right at the hotel and deliver it to the airport for you for $5 per bag or $15 per family on the day of your departure (or the day before if you have an early morning flight). They'll give you a boarding pass, so you can go directly to the gate at the airport. Perhaps the best thing about this hotel is its restaurant, Dukes, which overlooks the pool area and beach. The food is outstanding, and the atmosphere is friendly and comfortable and very relaxing. The Hula Grill and Chucks also overlook the beach and are very nice. There are a lot of best things about this hotel. We've stayed there three or four times already and plan to stay there again.

<Author>K2GO
<Content>Great Location Just returned from a 3 night stay at this hotel to wrap up our 11 day vacation. This was our 5th stay at this hotel and albeit a short stay, it was well worth it.This is a very busy and noisy hotel, but what you pay for is location, location, location. This is one of 6-7 hotels located on Waikiki Beach and it is by far, the best spot. We have also stayed at the Hilton Hawaiian Village( Very nice resort) and that location does not come close to what you experience staying at the Outrigger.This hotel is also home to Dukes restaurant and bar. They offer decent prices for their breakfast and lunch buffet's and the food is quite good. You can not beat their salad bar!The rooms are nice and comfortable. We have stayed in every catagory of room from ocean front to city view. If you have the means to stay ocean front , then it is certainly beautiful but only if you have the money. Every room will offer you a view of the ocean and for the most part, upgrading does not really give you a better vantage point of the ocean ( unless you are ocean front). By paying more and upgrading, this will certainly move you closer towards the water but does not give you that much more to look at.About the noise...You will hear your neighbours talking, you will hear toilets flushing before you are awake, you will hear inconsiderate people talking, laughing and yelling late at night. This you can't control but is ever present. Keep in mind that this happens in most hotels/resorts.Overall if you are coming to Waikiki, be prepared for lots of people and lots of noise. I would not stay anywhere else because of the location on the beach and the atmosphere at this hotel. If you require a quiet and more laid-back type of holiday, then perhaps you should go to one of the other Islands in Hawaii.

<Author>SydneySimon
<Content>Awesome - BUT First off I must say that I picked the Outrigger on the beach after reading mostly good reviews regarding the hotel. Despite these we still felt that it sounded the best, not to mention it was the 4th most popular at the time.Now, my wife and I were on our honeymoon and we travelled 10 hours from Australia. We were really looking forward to a good rest and a sleep in for a day or two, after the stresses of wedding prep. Our flight arrived early morning so we were at the hotel by about 10am. The customer service anywhere you go is more than you can ask for.Ok, check in at the hotel is 3pm, but the staff found us a room (ocean view which we paid for) no problems. It was room 721. This is where I put in my only complaint about our experience. The hotels walls must be made of tissue paper. 6am the next morning we could hear every word spoken from the room next door like they were standing on our bed and talking. Then the cleaners start at about 7.30am in the hall ways and they can be heard quite clearly as well. THIS WAS OUR ONLY COMPLAINT. We quietly complained and were moved to room 1522, which had no common walls, without any fuss at all. You could still hear the cleaners in the morning, but it was much better.Another good thing about being on the 15th floor was that you could use the express lift which only goes to floors 14 to the penthouse, so I suggest you ask to be put on 14 or above if you can. The location is awesome, walking distance to really good shopping (and Ala Moana if your keen). It's on the best part of the beach also. There are washing machines and dryers for hotel guests to use and right near there is a small sandwich shop that makes pretty nice sandwiches for when you are all steaked out.Recommend: dolphin experience at sealife park, pay the 7 bucks for the guided tour of the Missouri, don't bother getting up early for the Arizona as the line will already be very long. We went around midday but no later, hire a car and explore, the Plantation Spa in the Penthouse and dinner at the Westin next door. Get the filet mignon with the chocolate and whiskey sauce, it's unbelievable. Well hope this helps in any way.

<Author>travellightMinnesota
<Content>Fine Hotel and Great Location We loved our stay here with our two college aged children who had friends staying in the area.Rooms themselves were in fine condition and ample sized with flawless service and efficiency.We got a partial ocean view room which was on the first floor. Only negative was that it overlooked the roof of the kitchen and exhaust fans from the restaurant blew cooking smells into our room from time to time.......rooms 129/130. Am sure the hotel would have accomdated us if we requested a change, but by the time we got settled it was not worth it.The hotel is on the prime section of Waikiki beach, if you move much in either direction to other hotels which advertise as Waikiki beachfront, there are breakwaters and you quite soon lose the dramatic views of Diamond Head which adds to the magic of this place.There are three hotels located in this prime location.......the classic pink Royal Hawaiian, Westin Mona Surfrider, and the Outrigger Waikiki. We got slightly better rates at the Outrigger and could not have asked for better rooms. The advantage of the other two are that they are great classic hotels with hyper-impressive lobbies and common areas......not sure of their room sizes or conditions. I would say if you were going for a short stay you might want to have the experience (at slightly higher rates and maybe less superior rooms) of staying in one of the other two classics. If you are staying longer (we stayed 7 nights) I would go with the Outrigger Waikiki.The beach at this location is crowded, but it is the best. We bought beach chairs and some small umbrellas at Wal-Mart and used them here and at other beaches when we toured Oahu.Great experience all around and would certainly recommend.

<Author>what_beach_next
<Content>Good beachfront central location.....but so so hotel room We stayed here for 10 nights as part of our trip away to get married. As you can imagine, I wanted the hotel to be special -especially since we were getting married during our time in Waikiki. I had hoped, since the hotel were aware we were in Hawaii to get married, we might get a nice token gesture - ie a room upgrade or a bottle of champagne on arrival- but instead we got a box of chocolates or tea or something, it was that insignificant I can't even remember what it was. I don't want to sound ungrateful or presume something nice to be given to us, but it would have been a nice gesture from the hotel. Overall, if you are staying in Waikiki for just one to three nights, I would recommend this hotel as it is good value for money compared to the other beachfront hotels. But any longer than that, I would recommend somewhere else - and that is solely based on the uncomfortable bed and the noisy room location we were given (even after requesting a quiet room!). The hotel itself was great, but it was the terrible uncomfortable bed that ruined it for us, and the request for a quiet room was ignored. If I visit Waikiki again, I would either try the Moana Surfrider which is just along the beach a bit, or the Royal Hawaiian which was next door. I haven't stayed in either of those, but I would hope their beds are much more comfortable, and when requesting a quiet room that you might actually get one. I would be tempted to try one of those hotels the next time I go as the area was great, and they are beachfront. I thought the Hilton Hawiian Village was a little too far out of the hub of it all. For value of money, the Outrigger Waikiki on the Beach was the best option for us at the time, as 10 nights in another hotel in the same area and beachfront, was so much more expensive. But our hotel room allocation, and the terrible bed will make me think twice about rebooking this hotel in future. Anyway, in more detail....... Hotel Room Request: Upon checkin I asked for a quiet room, on a higher floor. The lady said, yes you are booked in a quiet room. Well, I was very disappointed to be given a room right beside the elevator, and each night we were wakened with people coming in and out of the lifts at all hours. We are heavy sleepers and don't normally waken up easily, but this did disturb us frequently. The room was also on the side of The Cheescake Factory, so I can sympathise with the other people who also left reviews saying it was noisy with the balcony doors open - due to this we never spent anytime on the balcony and never kept the doors open. To be honest, I didn't want to get stressed over it or create an issue so I never asked for room move. Looking back, I should have done straight away! Hotel Room Size  Space: The room itself was quite a good size, and had plenty of wardrobe space to hang things up and also a big set of drawers. The bathroom was tiny, it never actually had a bath, just a shower cubicle. The decor was a bit tired and dated. The AC unit was noisy, and it did waken me up several times a night, clunking on and off. Hotel Room Cleanliness: It was kept clean, although I did feel on occassions that the shower hadn't been cleaned for a couple of days. But then, the lighting was so poor in the shower area I couldn't really tell (and I am sure neither could the cleaner). Hotel Room Bed: This was the worst part of the room......it was awful! So uncomfy it was unbelievable! It was tiny, I couldn't believe how small it was. Even by UK sizes of beds which are so much smaller than the American beds, this was more like a big single bed than a double! It was very small, and very soft so I never slept well at all. I think if we were there for a shorter time, ie 2 or 3 nights it wouldn't have been so bad, but 10 nights in such an uncomfy bed was terrible. Hotel Location: Great, couldn't be better! Right on the beach. Good area, within walking distance for shops, restaurants, night life and exploring. We rented a car several days to drive and explore the island, stopping off at all the lovely beaches on the way. Not far at all by car to North Shore, Pearl Harbour or the Windward Coast. We walked up to Diamond Head and took a taxi back down, the walk from the hotel all the way to the top of Diamond Head probably took around 1.5/2 hours but was well worth it, we took it easy on the way up taking in all the views, and started off early to avoid the mid-day sun. Hotel Staff: The concierge very helpful with restaurant bookings. The travel desk was also helpful with booking a rental car. Hotel Amenities: Pool area, kept clean and a nice size. A live band a couple of times we were there in Dukes. Towels are available at the Pool area each day. We used the internet access and it was fine. Restaurants/bars in hotel: Good we ate  drank at them all and they were fine, Dukes of course was better value.

<Author>Rush4
<Content>Great location  We just completed a 1 week stay at the Outrigger Waikiki on the Beach and had a great time. All the staff were helpful and friendly. We enjoyed the coolers of ice water with lemon  lime that was available during the day in the lobby - nice touch. The staff  services were top notch. We arrived during the end of a winter wind / rain storm, which was an unusual event. Restaurants: Dukes  the Hula Grill had to put up tarps to keep the wind  rain out of the restaurant, which was interesting, but not terrible. Not much you can do about the weather, you know? The tarps came down as soon as the weather cleared up.We had free breakfast at Dukes or Hula Grill included in our room price. Dukes had a good buffet - lots of choices and everything kept freshly stocked. At the Hula Grill we had our choice of items from the menu. The breakfast was good here too, but the service was lacking the one day we tried it for breakfast, so we just stuck with Dukes. We had dinner at Dukes once and Hula Grill twice - we actually preferred the Hula Grill over Dukes for the atmosphere and view (and the service was wonderful at dinner). All the pigeons running around and flying around Dukes were a bit unnerving. Especially when they flew  landed on the table (yuck!). We put up with the birds during breakfast , but twice in one day was too much. I guess they were part of the atmosphere (?). The food was excellent in both restaurants.Our room was on an upper floor with a partial ocean view . We enjoyed sitting on the patio  taking in the sights. The rooms on that side of the hotel (at least on our floor) are rectangular shaped and a bit smaller than the angled rooms across the hall, but our room was adequate for the 2 of us. It had so much closet space and dresser drawers! We did talk to a man who had a room across the hall, right behind the elevators. He said there was no noise from the elevators at all, but he could hear the fans from the Cheesecake Factory next door. This surprised us, as we were at such a high floor. I do wish there was more light in the dressing area of the bathroom. The lighting is all over the vanity area, and it is dark looking into the closet, and also hard to see if you style your hair  turn your back to the vanity to use a hand mirror to see the back of your head! Housekeeping kept the room tidy  clean, which was nice. We did hear faint noise occasionally (not even daily) from our neighbors and even from the street performers across from the hotel at night, but I think I only noticed because of reviews I had read that said the hotel was very noisy. Although the rooms aren't completely soundproof, we didn't think it was too bad at all. We didn't rent a car, so we didn't have to experience the parking fees. We did enjoy the central location of the hotel - so easy to get anywhere we wanted to go! We had a late evening flight home, so we were able to have a late checkout (only 1 extra hour, but better than nothing) and we were able to use a courtesy room to clean up a bit before our trip home. That was a huge plus in our book! We would definitely stay here again!

<Author>Tex07
<Content>Great location This was my third stay at the Outrigger. I travel to Hawaii on business once or twice a year. The Outrigger has a lot going for it. It's right on the waikiki beach. It's got a great bar in Dukes. It's got a great resturant in the Hula Grill. Chucks steakhouse isn't very good, so skip it. It's right next door to the Cheescake factory if you're into that type of thing. Right across the street is a large open air international market place for buying all your Hawaii junk. When my wife was with me last February, I ponied up for a beachfront view. You have to be careful booking here. They oceanfront view, ocean view, partial ocean view and city view. I had the ocean view on my Feb trip, but it really was a lame view. So I upgraded to the best they had and it was nice. My wife is picky, God love her, and it met with her approval. This week I just got the el cheapo city view and it was in the far back corner of floor 10. No real complaints, but the bathroom was about the smallest I've ever seen in any hotel anywhere. (and I stay 75-100 nights on the road each year). But if you are looking for a $200/night hotel in Waikiki, this is about as good as it gets with the location. Negatives would be the upsell they always try on you when you check in. The pool is tiny, but hey you're on the beach. God's pool is steps away. Chucks Steakhouse had the worst of steaks. Pass on it. Waikiki is wall to wall tourists so be prepared. Some people dig it. I can only handle it for a night or two. Then I move on to the more quiet islands. Here's a tip if you're here in the winter and you dig watching pro's surf. Head to the north shore and find the Banzai Pipeline. Use a GPS. Good food in the little Q-hut across the street. Don't let Waikiki kill your love for Hawaii. Be sure to branch out to Maui or Kauai and see the real paradise. My favorite is the Wailea area of Maui. Whale watching during winter months is incredible. Right from the beach or check out the Pacific Whale Foundation and their eco-tours. Just incredible. Also, for what it's worth, before you come to Hawaii, be sure to read a good guide book, one that has some history of the islands. It really helps to understand the local hawaiian people. It helps you get insde their heads a bit and to be able to accept their aloha spirit. Hawaiians are amazing people. Get pas the tourist stuff and get to know them if you can. It's all an issue of respect and by reading up on the history of the islands, you will gain way more than you give. Mahalo!

<Author>bgm01
<Content>Great Place I think this is a great hotel. I disagree with a lot of the other reviews about noise and the lifts. We never had a problem with noise. We could not hear anything from the rooms next door and we were there for 5 nights. The lifts - we never waited more than a minute for the lifts to arrive and they were never full when they did arrive. We had a very spacious room on the 8th floor that did not look dated or old. It had a very comfortable king size bed (we made a special request for this) a two seater lounge, a work desk and a huge bathroom. There was one issue with the bathroom and that being when in the shower it was rather dark because there is no light near the shower and the shower curtin is very thick there for not letting any light in. Not a major problem at all. The hotel is in the best spot right on the beach, you walk out the back door and your on the sand. We walked up and down the beach each evening and some of the more expensive hotels have nowhere in front of the hotel whereyou can lay on the beach, some don't even have a beach, it's all rocks. I noticed a few people on here complain about the pool. Why would you use the pool when you have such a beautiful beach right in front of you? It's a safe beach too, small waves and no dangerous currents. We loved sitting on the balcony each evening with a beer or a glass of wine watching the turtles swimming and the surfers surfing. The view and sunsets are to dye for. We upgraded from a partial ocean view room to an ocean view room, they offered this to us on check in and we were glad we got a better room, we had to pay for it though. I am sorry if I have offended anyone but I now realise how lucky we are in Australia to have great tasting fresh food. We also made use of the little sandwich shop under the hotel. It's cheap and they make your sandwich fresh on the spot. There was no mini bar in our room but I think that was a good thing becausewe all know how inflated mini bar prices are in hotels. There is an ABC store right across from the hotel so you can get everything you need form there. In summary this is a top hotel, it's in a great spot, it has great views,the rooms are very comfortable and the staff are friendly.

<Author>sirrealone
<Content>Great place to finish off our honeymoon We went to Maui and then Oahu for our honeymoon. The travel agent recommended the Outrigger because it was right in the middle of everything and had a great beach location. He didn't lie. We were really impressed with the hotel. When we pulled up, we were told that the valet service was mandatory and would cost $25 per day. Our agent had told us that mandatory parking charges were now becoming the norm, and this didn't take us much by surprise, though I thought $25 per day was a bit extravagent. However, one nice feature is that we didn't even have to take our bags out of the car. They offered to do it for us. At check in, I was impressed that you sit down to do your paperwork and reservation information. I've been in a number of hotels, and this was a nice touch. They offered to upgrade us from a city view room to an ocean view room for around $100 per night. We said we'd like to see the city room first. When we got there, we were pleased to see that we could still see the ocean from our room. I had thought city view meant that we'd be along the street side, but they really don't have any rooms facing the street...instead we were on the side facing another hotel, but you could still see the ocean. I was impressed when the bags showed up almost immediately after we walked into the room. Very quick with those! The room was nice. We had a king bed which was comfortable, though the pillows are not very fluffy. The decor was tasteful. All of the amenities were nice. Because we were on our honeymoon, they sent up a bottle of champagne. I can't remember if it was waiting for us, or if it was sent separate, but that was nice. They include two bottles of water in the in-room fridge, but I was surprised when they didn't re-stock those daily, as they had in our hotel in Maui. The pool isn't much to speak of, but the beach is great. The swimming in front of the hotel and neighboring hotels is among the most popular, as judged by the number of people in the water. Still, we never felt overcrowded while swimming or sitting by our towels. If you plan on going to the beach and not renting one of their umbrellas, I'd plan on grabbing some towels from the towel stand (at the pool) and then setting up in front of the Pink Palace hotel, which is next door. The reason for this is that the Outrigger sets up people with their umbrellas almost all the way to the shoreline, and you'll find it very awkward to navigate around them. The Pink Palace isn't as close to shore, so their umbrella area is set back and this gives a big area for people. We noticed a lot of other Outrigger guests discovered the same thing.The restaurants are very good. We did not go to the steak house. Nor did we dine at the Hula Grill (we'd already dined at one in Maui), though we did stop in for Happy Hour, which as excellent drinks at reasonable prices from 3-6pm. We had the breakfast buffet at Duke's, which is awesome and well worth the $14.95 price. During happy hour on Friday, Saturday, and Sunday, they have a live band playing outside that you can hear from the beach, pool, and the restaurants. They play some nice relaxing yet fun music. Unfortunately we checked in on Sunday so we only got one day to enjoy this. As I mentioned the service at the hotel was great. The concierge was very helpful in making sure we knew the ins and outs of the island, and also recommended routes and times for various activities. The housekeeping service is also very good. We had one problem, but they went above and beyond to correct it. Before we left the hotel for the morning, we called and requested cleaning to take place during the hours we'd be gone. They said it'd be no problem, yet when we got back it had not been cleaned. However, I saw the cleaning staff on the floor and figured they were just running behind. Yet, around 5pm we were disappointed to return to the room and see that it'd not been cleaned. I called down and the operator told me that according to their records, it'd been cleaned. When I assured her that it hadn't, she was very apologetic and said that it must have been checked off incorrectly. Within 2-3 minutes someone arrived to change our towels and quickly make up our bed. Five minutes after that, they called again to ask what time we'd be going to dinner because they wanted to do a full cleaning. Sure enough when we got back from dinner, they'd fully cleaned the room and left a giant basket of various treats on the dresser. The next day, they called to make sure everything had been done, AND to ask what times we'd like the room cleaned for the remaining days we'd be guests. We were quite pleased at how they went above and beyond to correct their mistake. The valet did get the car within 2 minutes of request every time that we went down, even when we checked out, which was a crazy time due to tons of people checking in because of some big festival taking place that weekend. They also allowed us to check out at 1pm rather than noon, which allowed us to leave at the perfect time to head to the airport.This was a great hotel that I would recommend to anybody.

<Author>SDChargers_fan
<Content>It's all about the beach, cause the hotel is average Just the wife and myself on the anniversary for 8 days. A few years ago, we stayed at the Sharaton Waikiki 300 yards away. There hotel was great, but it lacked direct beach frontage. At that time, I noticed the pleasant access of Outrigger Hotel's beach front location and view from Dukes restaurant, and opted for it this go around. Its really hard to screw up the day activities at Waikiki beach, so I will only mention the bad aspects of the time we were actually in the hotel. They charged $25/night to park your car with no discount to hotel guests. This was not divulged on web site. While the hotel web site indicates that it matters, actually selecting (or in my case verbally requesting) the ocean view/king bed and then getting it upon arrival are two diff things. Upon arrival, they suggested that next time I should call up a day or two before arrival to remind them. For a minute there, I could almost swear that some palm scratching was in order/required, if you get my drift. Fortunately, significant begging did the trick, after I declined to pay for their offer of an ocean front upgrade room. What I got was the room across from the elevator. While the elevator is not noisy, the people traffic is. Without a doubt, (and as everyone else writes) the walls are paper thin. A door closing nearby is a loud bang. The Air conditioning unit is loud on high, and fidgety to maintain on low. The toilet flushes so loud, Al Bundy would be proud of its power. Above you, below you, next to you. If your the party animal who can manage to stay up and continue the cocktail'ing in your room, then this is no big deal to you. If you are like us and enjoy somewhat of a peaceful night starting at 9 - 10pm, then you wont dig this. Very simply, normal talking can be heard from adjacent rooms and from across the hall. As indicated, our first room was next to/across from the elevator. Two days later, we requested and received a relocation. Now we were next to the lady with the hearing aid (literally) and loud TV at night. Called building security and they eventually got her to turn it down. The Hula grill and Chuck's Steak House are the alternate restaurants but they are not open for lunch. This limits you to Dukes, which is OK at best. Honestly, the $2.50 pre-fab tuna sandwich in the lobby market comes with light mayo and is a very tasty night snack. The $6 tuna sandwich for lunch from the lobby custom deli (closes at 5pm) sucked due to them soaking it with mayo. My fault. I still recommended the deli over Dukes for an economy lunch. For the budget minded drunk, I recommend going to the ABC market across the street and buying 10 of the $1.50 bacardi mini-bar bottles. Get the free (or low cost) passion/guava mix from the bar and bingo, instant Mai Tai. Excellent. I know, I'm a cheap sh**. But it saved me $300 bucks! I also recommend that upon arrival, ask the beach services desk to give you one of the free rafts that everyone leaves there. Otherwise, go to ABC store and but one for $2. If you want chairs and umbrella, same thing. Buy it at ABC. Otherwise, rentals for each item is $5 - $50 day. Then throw it away when you done. Overall rating - Average.

<Author>herv_7
<Content>a very good hotel in an excellent location We spent 6 nights in the hotel and overall it was a very nice experience. We chose this hotel as it had good reviews in tripadvisor, was reasonably priced and next to the waikiki beach. We had made a reservation for a partial ocean view room and got a ....partial ocean view room. The room itself was very nice, clean had a comfortable king size bed. The balcony was a little bit small for our taste, though.We tasted the food at two restaurants in the hotel, the grill and the dukes. The dukes is a little bit noisy and extremely busy during breakfast time, however at lunch time the buffet is a steal at 13 USD per person. The grill is fine for breakfast and reasonably priced if you choose a light continental breakfast rather than a full american one.The pool is nice, however there is not enough space for people looking for a shadowy place. Also , the beach towels are very thin and should be replaced by new ones.The beach is wonderful, however you have to pay up to 50 USD to get two beach chairs with an umbrella. I heard that this kind of service is free in some other hotels, so consider this when you compare prices within hotels of similar category. Concerning the hotel itself, it's a little bit outdated and does not have the charm or the elegance of its two neighbours (the royal hawaian and the westin) but considering the price, the outrigger is probably a better deal. The location is perfect and you are close to everything.Overall, we spent a wonderful vacation in Hawai and if you cannot (like us) spend more than 250 USD a night, this the right place to goThe only real complaint is that the walls are paper thin. So be nice with your neighbours.

We didn't eat there, but went to some very good restaurants in the vicinity though namely Hy's steakhouse  Top of Waikiki which offers panoramic views of the area whilst turning you 360 degrees in an hour! The Outrigger is in need of some updating it looks a little tired, but really does have a great location, probably the best in the area. Everything is at your fingertips from the beach to the shops to the restaurants. We ended up bringing another suitcase home full of new clothes as they have 2 great shopping malls in Ala Moana  Waikele. We hired a car  went round the island in a day, the North Shore beaches are a nice drive  worth going to. On the whole I probably wouldn't return to the Outrigger however it does offer value for money. Honolulu is a great place to go for a few days though I would jet off to nearby islands if staying for a bit longer! You will also come across an unbelievable amount of japanese tourists in Hawaii which I found amazing as they simply overrun the city! All very harmless though  very tend to leave the beaches to tattoo clad surfers  sun worshippers!

<Author>OC-Lynch
<Content>Best Hotel in Waikiki We stayed at the Outrigger Waikiki the week of July 25-31. We checked in pretty early and our room wasn鈥檛 ready yet, so the staff put a rush on it. We grabbed some coffee and snacks from Seattle鈥檚 Best located at the entrance of the hotel and within 20 minutes our room was ready. When making our reservations, we requested a room on the Diamond Head side and on a high floor. They honored all our requests and gave us a complimentary room upgrade from a city view to a partial ocean view. We were on the 15th floor, which gave us access to the express elevators that only service floors 14, 15  PH. There are some rooms located right it next to the express elevators and I鈥檓 sure it can get pretty noisy right there. Luckily for us, we were a good distance from any of the elevators, so we had no problems. We did hear the sounds of toilets flushing a few times, but that鈥檚 only because the toilets pack a powerful flush, which in my opinion is a good thing. The noise from the toilets never bothered us or woke us up. Other than that, we never heard any noise coming from any of the other rooms, so the walls aren鈥檛 as thin as others described. The room itself is nicely furnished. The bathroom has granite countertops and there is plenty of closet space and drawers. The lani fit me, my husband and our 10 year old daughter comfortably for breakfast, although we did leave our sliding door open for a little extra space. One of the best things about this hotel is that it鈥檚 located right smack in the middle of everything. The International Marketplace is across the street and the Royal Hawaiian Shopping center is just around the corner. Not to mention it houses one of the best restaurants in all of Waikiki鈥ukes. Dukes is reasonably priced, has great food  drinks, and has one of the best views of Waikiki. Try the Lava Flow, you鈥檒l be addicted! We also ate at Hula Grill for dinner, which also has great views of Waikiki. Room service is provided by Hula Grill. The chocolate chip pancakes were delicious!The beach right outside the hotel is beautiful. There is always something to do on the beach. Whether it be a catamaran sail, canoe ride, surfing lessons, or just floating in the ocean, the Outrigger has everything within arms reach. The on-site restaurants and some of the activities allow you to charge the costs to your room, which came in very handy as we hardly ever had to carry cash on us. You can rent 2 beach chairs  an umbrella for $30-$50 a day, depending on what type of chair you want. Rent your chairs early so you can get a good spot on the beach. Make sure to buy inflatable rafts or intertubes at the ABC store across the street. This will make for a wonderful time in the ocean.The pool was a bit small for such a big resort, but we were always able to find a spot. It鈥檚 illegal to drink alcohol on the beach, but since this hotel is right on the beach, you could drink by the pool overlooking the ocean and still have the same feel. I cannot say enough about the great staff. They were all so friendly and attentive. We needed towels before the towel desk opened and housekeeping quickly brought them up to our room. If you renting a car, getting into the hotel can be a little bit of a wait at times, but very too bad. The valets are really good about getting everyone in  out as quickly as possible. Everyday housekeeping leaves a newsletter in your room listing the activities the hotel offers such as lei making.The Outrigger was one of the best hotels I鈥檝e ever stayed at and if and when we return to Oahu, we will definitely return to the Outrigger Waikiki on the Beach. If you鈥檙e looking for a nice quiet vacation, then this hotel is not for you, but if you鈥檙e looking for a beautiful hotel in the middle of all the action, then this is definitely the place for you.Aloha!

<Author>LillianLM
<Content>Can't beat the location! Our family, comprised of 2 adults in our late 40's and 2 teenage boys, just returned from a great 4 night stay at the Outrigger in Waikiki. We were extremely pleased with the hotel. The layout of the lobby is interesting and works very well -- the ground floor in the street exit, with an activities desk, retail shops, a coffee place and Dukes. The check-in is on the second floor, which effectively separates the folks checking in and out from the other goings-on in the lobby. When we checked in, the woman working the desk tried very hard to sell us on an upgrade from a city-view room to a partial ocean view for only $69 per room night (we had 2 rooms). When we turned her down, she smiled and said she'd talk to her manager and then came back, whispering that her manager agreed to upgrade us by giving us 2 partial ocean view rooms but charging us for only one. We also turned that down (I mean, I don't stay in the room except to sleep and we were going to stay in ocean-front condos on Maui and the Big Island, so I felt it wasn't necessary.) I felt as though I was buying car with that experience, but that was the only negative experience and it was minor. The staff was extremely friendly and we found the rooms to be extremely clean and well laid out. We had 14th floor, city view rooms. The 14th and 15th floor have their own elevator, which is very handy, as I noticed the other elevators were always packed. I would take care NOT to have a city-view room on a lower floor, as the fans on the roof of the building next door (Cheesecake Facory) are noisy if you're clser than we were. I would also take care NOT to get a room right next to the elevators. The pool and the beach in front of the hotel are very crowded but Waikiki, in general, is very crowed. The hotel's location is in the heart of things. We always went to breakfast on the road parallel to the street the hotel is on -- there are a variety of places to go. The local shopping became very upscale from the last time I was in Waikiki 20 years ago. You can find Prada, Cartier, Tiffany, Baly, etc. intermixed with cheap t-shirt shops and loads of ABC stores. All in all, I recommend this hotel and would stay here again if returning to Waikiki.

The International market place which is situated across from the hotel is awful too- oh my god I have never seen so many stores selling such rubbish. We did go to see the rest of the island which is a must other wise you would just think the whole island is concrete and high rise buildings. It is such a shame I think the place has been ruined and a million miles away from the paradise we expected. If you are looking for paradise I would try another island or go somewhere totally different. The only good thing about the place was the Hulla Grill, happy hour at the Hulla Grill was fab and the staff really friendly. Cocktails are fab too!

<Author>johnsmith47
<Content>Excellent Hotel with small beach and poor soundproofing My wife and I stayed at the Outrigger Waikiki for 5 days at the end of May. We booked the hotel through Expedia, finding a much better deal on that site than booking through the hotel's web site, which was slow, and confusing. Expedia allowed me to combine discounts that the hotel reservations didn't offer. Our package included free breakfast every day, which was terrific, and a car, which we wished we had skipped. The hotel staff was excellent. Everyone was friendly and helpful, including the valet guys and bell staff. Service was always prompt. The property was very well maintained. Our room had an ocean view, with a very small balcony. The room was large, with space for a couch and a desk with 2 chairs. The hotel provides free calling anywhere in the US, something I have never found anywhere else and free wired internet access. Most higher end properties charge for these services, and I have never stayed in a hotel with free toll calling. There are 2 problems with this hotel--a very small beach and poor soundproofing. We met an elderly lady who was badly sunburned. She said you had to be on the beach by 8:00 am to get an umbrella on the beach. There is a small strip of land and a small deck. If you come down later in the morning, you're basically out of luck, but judging the size of other hotels on waikiki, you're probably out of luck everywhere by that time. However, with a strong tropical sun, unless you're already deeply tanned, you won't be able to spend much time without shade. The water is great, with a sandy shallow area, followed by a deeper dropoff for about 50 yards and then a sandy shallow reef. You can swim or paddle out to the reef on a raft and float around through the waves.Breakfast was great. We really enjoyed eating in the open air restaurant every day when it opened at 6:30.We rented a car, but wasted our money doing so. There is transportation everywhere you would want to go. Parking is valet only for $25 per day. There are plenty of places to rent cars for the day or two you might want to drive somewhere else on the island. We went to the luau at the Sheraton Royal Hawaiian, the Pink Palace next store. It was expensive, but the food was good and the show was great.The only real downside to the hotel was the terrible soundproofing. I am a light sleeper and was awakened twice late at night by the sound of the couple in the next room making whoopee, and by the sound of the guests using their bathrooms at other times in the night. We could also hear muffled conversations in the adjoining rooms in the morning. I have usually found that hotels in this price range are pretty quiet. This one needs some work to cut down on the sound intrusion in the rooms. That said, I would stay here again, but bring soft ear plugs.The restaurants have free music, including a live band on the beach side deck on the weekends, which draws a lively crowd.The bar has a very good happy hour. The bartenders are first rate. Watch out for the Mai Tai. When they warn you about them, take heed. Meal prices on the hotel are good for Waikiki. To save money, go one block over to Kuhio Ave, where the less expensive restaurants are, or take the bus to Ala Moana shopping center, a few blocks away. Also walk up to Kapiolani Park a few blocks toward Diamond Head. We found a little festival on the weekend, with music and local food vendors, including one selling Hawaian food.Yes Waikiki is overdeveloped, crowded and touristy. But swim out to the reef, look toward Diamond Head, and have breakfast on the veranda watching the rainbow through the clouds and the surfers on the reef and you'll know why this you came.

<Author>portnoyd
<Content>Perfect Oahu honeymoon hotel We stayed at the Outrigger Waikiki on the Beach from April 16th to the 22nd on our honeymoon. This was our first trip to Hawaii. We stayed in an Oceanfront Deluxe Room with Whirlpool Tub.Pros: Insane view and beach location, nice and well done hotel room, ideal Waikiki locationCons: Lot of foot traffic through hotel due to Duke's and Kalakaua Ave, very mediocre room serviceOverall, we see no reason to ever try another hotel in Waikiki, should we (hopefully) return. The Outrigger offers you all you really need out of a Waikiki hotel. First, the room itself was nice, well kept, and in good repair. The whirlpool tub wasa good size. Not huge, but could comfortably fit 2 people in it. (You want a huge one? Portofino Hotel in Redondo Beach, CA -call up and ask for one of those rooms - you won't be disappointed!) The room size is good for two as is thevanity/bathroom area. For some reason, our toilet would periodically partially self-flush itself. Amusing but never a bother.Yes, this room setup is expensive, but being as we were going on our honeymoon, all caution to the wind.As mentioned, we had an oceanfront room and it lived up to its name. It really was something I couldn't get over. This is more of a general comment, as I'm sure you can get the same view from other beachfront hotels. It is worth spending the moneyif you can afford it. With that, be sure to get a room above the 6th or 7th floor. It will help minimize the noise as well asincrease your view. We were on the 8th and it was just right.The staff was friendly and helpful, even though we didn't use them all too often. We went to the activity desk once but decided against scubaing in Oahu. If you like shows, the Society of Seven is there but I couldn't even tell you what it'sabout. We did 1 1/2 days of shopping/Pearl Harbor, then laid worthless on the beach the rest of the time. Amen.Previous reviewers had mentioned the noise in their review, and it's true in some regards. We never heard our neighbors the entire trip, but the music is noticable at night. However, any beachfront hotel in that section is going to fall victim to it, and I find it unlikely any hotel in Waikiki can dodge it - either entertainment or sheer volume from the shops and roads in the area. Remember, you're not coming to Waikiki to completely get away - it's a tourist trap. (But one of the best ones you can experience) Save any one of the other islands for that. Doesn't mean you can't lay on the beach all day, but you won't get the peace of Maui though.Room service was purchased on the first night, and that was the last time we used it. The burgers were near charcoal, few fries, and generally a waste of money. Skip it and run out to ABC or something for provisions if you want to stay in. ABC - no matter where you are in Waikiki, there are least 7 stores in short walking distance. Room service is provided by the Hula Grill, so I would say skip them. We never went to Chuck's, but we did go to Duke's several times.We couldn't figure out what the big deal was. Breakfast was standard; a nice buffet. Lunch was standard. Dinner, however, was disappointing. The menu is quite small, and nonexistent if you don't like or don't feel like eating fish. It's not a bad place, but it certainly is not something you should make a point in visiting. However, if you do like Duke's, you can wait out any seating wait times up in your hotel room, and they'll call you down. A nice touch. You also have Cheesecake Factory right next door if you choose, but keep in mind it's Cheesecake Factory and always mobbed. Other restaurants abound, including every fast food place you can want. I highly recommend the Kalua Pig Quesdillas from the Red Lion Restaurant!We did not rent a car so we cannot speak of valet/parking costs. You basically want to take The Bus everywhere with a cab for more direct stops. The airport, Pearl Harbor, and Ala Moana Center are all we used it for. The zoo and aquarium is only a mile down Kalakaua, and you should make that walk because it has some nice sights.Now, the important part: the beach. It is not incredibly big, but we could see from our view that it was one of the bigger ones on this stretch of Waikiki. One thing that separates it from the other beachfront hotels is apparent early in the day from our view. The Outrigger beach section leads into a coral free part of the ocean that will take you out to the surfing area. If you look at the Sheraton to your left and the big pink eyesore to your right, it's mostly coral a few feet out into the ocean. It's nice to be able to walk out a football field's distance and still be in the water up to your waist.The beach rental costs were standard so be prepared for that added cost. Definitely rent them as your spot will be reserved even if you are gone half the day. The guys in the rental booth may try and pawn their lotions off on you and let me tell you: if you get burned, take the two they offer you. Works miracles. I really thought they would be worthless but the pain relief was astounding (this from the guy who got burned on the second day, and then reburned at least 3 more times... ow). So don't take offense; they are actually selling some useful product.In the morning, be sure to go down a little before 8am and drop some towels on the spot you want, THEN rent your chairs. I learned this the hard way the last day when the last open front spot got taken by some mook and his kids right before me. Also, try and stay to the left and right of the canoe docks, as the catamarans will come and block your view a few times a day if positioning the wrong spot.Other than that, there isn't much more for us to speak of. If you can afford it, it's the right choice for a Waikiki getaway.

<Author>ljinhawaii
<Content>Excellent location! Great beach We stayed at OW from Sunday, April 29 to Wednesday, May 2 after a week long cruise on the Pride of Aloha with Norweigan cruise lines. We did have a partial view of the ocean and a nice balcony (just had to ignore the fans a few floors below and across the way). We got some great night time shots there of the streets and buildings below, so that was good. One problem we did encounter was the awful squeak of the service elevator hallway door. It drove me nuts and I wore my earplugs the first night. I wrote on their comment card the next day what they could do to make my stay better was to oil the squeaky door hinges. The next day it was done! No more squeaking so I was mighty impressed by that. I was also impressed with the free long distance to the U.S. and Canada (yes we're from Canada and it was absolutely free from Hawaii no hidden charges) and the internet was free, although slow at times. We brought our own laptop. We also got postcards in our package from the front desk and they said they would mail them anywhere in the world. So I took advantage of that too and mailed my grandmother back home (good for people who are not on the internet). Yes the walls are thin, but I haven't been to many busy hotels where I haven't heard noise from people next door. Having a fridge was great too. We bought bottles of wine from the store downstairs and fit nicely.The main pluses of this hotel are the view, it's proximity to the wonderful beach and also Diamond head (So pretty at sunset). We hiked from the hotel to the summit on our last day. It was a long walk all uphill. Took about 2 hours to get to the crater. We took the bus back which runs every half hour or so from the base (We'd had enough exercise). You can also take the city bus from Kuhio St one block over and pay $2 to go to the Dole Plantation or the north shore. It's a long ride 1 1/2 to 2 hours, but it saves so much money. You can get a bus map from the ABC store. You can snorkel just around the backyard of the hotel and see many different fish. One guy I talked to even saw giant sea turtles there the day before. We went to the International marketplace across the street many times. Great place for souvenirs. ABC Stores have the best prices for Mauna Loa macadamia nuts. All in all it is a great place to go. Keep in mind that Waikiki is a busy city. Not a relaxing, peaceful place for vacation.We recommend it, but request a room away from the fans if noise bothers you.

<Author>cdar
<Content>Perfect Location The location is perfect, IF you want to be in the center of the action. You're only steps from shopping, restaurants, entertainment, and the beach. My husband and I were travelling with our two teenaged girls. We had a lovely 4th floor city view room on the diamond head side; we could see the ocean as well as the guests in the hotel next door. The room had two double beds (small) and a hide a bed. While there was enough room when you were just hanging out, it did get a bit crowded when we were getting ready to go out. The walk-in closet/dressing area included the vanity and sink , a sliding door seperated the toilet and shower (the tub was maybe 2 ft x 2 ft). My husband and I have no trouble sharing this area; however the teenages did; and went one at a time. Our vacation had started off at Turtle Bay, which was a beautiful large room and dressing area, and view. The Outrigger just does not compare. I expect I would have loved the Sheraton next door; but not the price! Therefore the Outrigger does win out! We alternated beach days and activity days. Days on the beach included surf lessons on the left side of the hotel, there were also ones to the right. We chose semi-private lessons which worked out very well. Loved the catamaran sail that left from the Outrigger Reef ($10 off coupon in the book they give you on check in., as well as coupons for some of the stores close to the hotel). We rented a car from Hertz just accross the street on the days we did activities. Budget located there too. It was cheaper for our family to rent a car than to go on a orgaized tour and it gave us the freedom to move on when we felt like it, stop whenever for lunch or a view. Our girls loved the Royal Swim at Sea Life Park, ear to ear grins on all participants in that program. We went very early to Hanama Bay, but the water was not very clear. We chose the late day admission and show package at the Polynesian Cultural Center; this was in the brochure I picked up at the airport. We did this out of Turtle Bay; and it was enough time for our family. We enjoyed all our meals. Most mornings we had a large breakfast and only needed an early evening meal. Favorites were breakfast at Duke's, another morning we went to the Pink Palace (the experience, view, and service alone was worth the slightly higher price, if you can do it liesurely, the girls ordered hot chocoate and it came in individal teapots and a bowl of whipped cream). The Cheesecake Factory has fantastic food and there is a lot of it; most of the time we saw people waiting to get in. The California Pizza Kitchen across the street has wonderful thin crust pizza's, reasonably priced, however the balcony view is of the construction going on at the Royal Hawaiin Shopping Center! (Not much open in there yet). There is also one at the AlaMoana shopping center. While the girls watched an inroom movie my husband and I went to the Moana beach bar for a drink and appetizer. Lovely view and a local band. It's much quieter than Duke's. The worst thing about the Outrigger is the noise. At times I just wanted some quiet. We could hear the bands outside, the music was Duke's was pleasant, however one of the street buskers was just a pounding on a drum with very little rythum which seemed to go on for hours. Attempts to drown it out by turning on the fan in the room helped, you had to keep turning it on again and again as it must be on a timer. Fortunately we were from an earlier time zone and we up early every day to take advantage of the daylight hours, because you can hear everyone flushing toilets, showering, baby crying several doors down. At certain times of days, the elevator wait was long. We gave up and took the stairs from the 4th floor. You either chose the ones that took you to the beach (lower stairs are creepy, we met an uncomfortable lady who was glad to see us, because its still a couple more flights down than your floor number; or another set that opened to the lobby level.) The staff were wonderful at all times; always an Aloha in the hallways. The Waikiki Beach Walk is still in the works, but it doesn't look like much more than more hotels, restaurants, and more shopping. Some stores repeat themselves every few blocks or have similar stock (not Just ABC!, and ABC was not open at 7am when I desperately needed a second coffee to go!). I kept seeing the same bathing suits, flip flops over and over. Stores are everywhere, many upscale ones and some fun ones in the International Market Place and they are open very late. Macy's was open till 11pm every night including Easter Sunday. We had lots of luggage and the hotel just made sure we got one of the large van type taxi's to take us back to the airport. We didn't have to pre-book or anything. But the taxi only took cash, and we are very dependent upon credit cards. So there went the rest of the US cash, but the food places at the airport take credit cards so all was good. We would definately consider staying at the Outrigger again.

<Author>MyBestTripEver
<Content>Very Nice Place We stayed at the Outrigger Waikiki for 7 nights while on our honeymoon. I had read all the reviews for months in advance about different hotels including this one just because I wanted the trip to go well for our first experience to Hawaii. We had a city view room but it still had a nice view of the ocean. The room is good enough, the bed was smaller than I had expected, but honestly we were only there late at night. You can hear your neighbors but it was no different than apartments I have lived in with shared walls. If you have extra wild neighbors they will keep you up. The only thing we really heard was a toilet flush every so often.  The bathroom is okay, that's where the fridge was for us, under the sink. The shower is tiny, not much fun for two, it's basically 1/3rd of a bath, if you can call it a bath. We had a couch in our room and a decent balcony facing the ocean. It was never crowded in the hotel and I was surprised that we didn't have to wait for check-in.  We never had to wait for the elevators for more than 30 seconds. The staff were very nice especially since we had to leave our luggage at the hotel since our flight out was very late. We didn't eat at the hotel. It's hawaii and we didn't want to eat where we were staying, we wanted to see more of Waikiki. Dukes is right there with a nice view and seemed very popular. We didn't play in the pool. Why travel across the world and play in the pool and not the ocean?  The best thing about the hotel was the location. Very easy access to the beach, ocean and shopping. The beach is crowded but there is always space to relax. The hotel is in the middle of the action and everything is close.  We really didn't spend a lot of food. It was actually a lot cheaper than I had planned at the start of the trip. If you want to spend a lot of money you can, if you want to save a little you can as well. There are lots of little shops and businesses and smaller restaurants that don't cost a fortune. Every single restaurant that I'm used to seeing here in my hometown is also with-in a few blocks of the hotel. Honestly we just grabbed bagels, yogurt and fruit in the morning as we headed out on a tour or to the beach. Plus you have ABC convenience stores about every 30 feet that have all the basics. We mainly ate at luau's or even a few homes of the hawaiin's who invited us to dinner one night which was fun! We never rented a car the whole time and we were really glad. Waikiki is a busy place and we used buses to get to tours and travel the island. We had tours set up and the bus was included in the travel. We caught those just a block away behind the Hyatt hotel when we went to the North Shore, Polynesian Cultural Center, and Snorkling or to the Luau's. We took the city bus when we hiked Diamond Head. You can go anywhere on the bus for just $2 which is nice. I wouldn't recommend traveling to the North Shore this way, but if you just want to go a few miles or less in Waikiki then it's better than driving. Just get a bus map from the activities desk and it has all the routes listed and what buses to take. We really got to enjoy a lot of activities. We toured the whole island from top to bottom and loved it. We just planned one fun thing a day and lined it up the day we got there and had our tickets for everything. We went on the tour, shows, or snorkling in the morning and then had the afternoons to lay out, shop or just relax. But do things quick or you will miss out and waste your time there. The stuff we really enjoyed were Captain Bob's Snorkling and the luau's. They only take 40 people a day on a catamaran for Captain bob's and go to a sand bar where you can practice your skills or play volleyball in the ocean. Then you have a BBQ and set out to a reef. It was so much fun and my wife took some fish food and we were surrounded by tons of fish, it was impressive and a lot of fun. We also enjoyed Germaine's Luau. It was a good show and the food wasn't bad either. You should also play on another beach like the North Shore or another part of the island, if you don't leave Waikiki you will be missing out!  The weather was perfect. 82 for a high and 70 at night. I traveled home with shorts and sandals and arrived back to snow on the ground!  Sorry there aren't photos, we took a ton, but we're just married and life is hectic and photos are last on the list to get done right now.

<Content>Ruined my Honeymoon!! Where to start? We arrived in Honolulu Thursday 3/15/07 to prepare for our Sunday wedding. We stayed at the Hilton Hawaiian Village with no issues. That night I called the Outrigger Waikiki on the beach to confirm our request for a king bed and partial ocean view. The first time I called the operator accidentally hung up on me. The second call I was transferred to nowhere and the line rang for minutes. The third call, I was told quite rudely that my reservation had been canceled. The hotel refused to give me any more information and said I had to deal with the booking agency. It took two days to sort out, and instead of enjoying all the festivities leading up to the wedding I spent the time worrying about where we'd stay for the honeymoon. It turns out the hotel had my first and last names switched, and I had proof that it was booked correctly.When we arrived at the hotel, the staff was cold and unwelcoming. Our room was wrong, as they had given us two double beds instead of the king we had requested months ago. We were supposed to have chilled champagne and treats waiting for us in the room and that didn't happen either. When I contacted the hotel the woman I spoke to argued with me about what came with my package. I had all the correct paperwork and was perfectly willing to show here, but she said fine! and slammed sown the phone. It was in the room waiting for us when we got back from dinner- warm, with no treats. The room smelled old and dingy. The furniture was dusty and by the look of the bathroom we were happy that we brought Clorox wipes. We were on a low floor and our balcony door didn鈥檛 lock, so we had to lock up all our belongings well anytime we left the room and hoped the bags would be there when we got back. And no, the hotel did not do anything to help us with this one either.The walls are very, very thin. We were woken up every morning by 6 AM by doors slamming, children running around, and adults talking. The first morning at 5 AM a school-aged boy was screaming so loud and painfully we called security because we were scared. It turns out that nothing was wrong and he did that a lot. That was for the first two days. The second two days had another family next to us with a bunch of kids crowded into the room. We could hear everything. We kept our privacy please sign on the door at all times when we were in the room, but housekeeping still knocked and woke us up. They did not take care to keep their voices down, even when they started at 8AM. I travel a lot, and this is the loudest hotel I've ever been in!!The room was booked under my maiden name, but we gave specific instructions when we checked in about our married name. The morning newsletter said welcome Mr. and Mrs. 'Maiden Name'! I was crushed because I wanted this for my scrapbook. I asked for them to change it and add it to the next morning's flyer. They complied, but were not nice about it.The first morning after the first night I went down to speak to the manager. We were exhausted and not enjoying our honeymoon at all, due solely to the Outrigger. I spoke to the Guest Services Manager, Brian, who looked and acted like he could not have cared less. He stared blankly at me while I explained our situation. He offered to move us, but could not accommodate our special needs (king bed, at least partial ocean view). I told him I wanted Outrigger to make a gesture to show that they appreciate our business and care that our honeymoon was being ruined. Even after telling him we like to sleep in and stay out late, he said the best he could do was breakfast coupons. I'm not complaining about getting something for free, but I wondered if he had heard anything I had said about sleeping in. In order to use the coupons we had to get up early. Good thing our thin walls helped us make it on time.There were other issues as the weeks progressed that I won't add, but the worst part is that I wanted to speak to another manager and never got the chance. I called and went to the front desk every day and the answer was always he's in a meeting or I'll have him call you. He (or she) never called and apparently is still in the meeting. Right before we left the hotel for the airport my new husband tried again. He had about as much luck as I did, but he was promised a personal letter of apology for all we experienced. I we do not receive that letter of apology we will report this hotel to the Better Business Bureau.The big picture of this hotel is very thin walls, unaccommodating staff, overcrowded with kids, and being told no everywhere you turn. I will never go back to this hotel, much less any Outrigger. We stayed also stayed at the Hilton Hawaiian Village and the JW Marriott Ihilani on this trip and had no issues whatsoever.
