<Author>LIBeachBum
<Content>Perfect Place on Waikiki We spent the first part of our honeymoon at the Outrigger and absolutely loved it. It's in the center of the strip so there are endless restaurants and bars to choose from within walking distance (don't let anyone talk you into renting a car, you'll never use it). We spent a lot of time in the restaurant located in the hotel called Duke's. The food is excellent and the bar is within easy walking distance to the beach. Unfortunately there is no drinking on the beach itself so you'll have to keep those Mai Tai's and Pina Colada's at the bar. As far as the food goes, we didn't have a bad meal once. They have a great buffet for breakfast and the usual lunch/dinner choices.The room was very nice but needed to be updated. We didn't spend all that much time in the room so it didn't really matter to us. The view, on the other hand, was perfect. We had a great view of the Pacific and a view of the street all from our balcony.When going to the beach I'd suggest waking up early and reserving your chairs and umbrellas. The hotel offers them right outside for a reasonable price. They go quickly though so make your claim early otherwise you'll be sitting in the sand.If your package includes an introduction to the islands where you can sign up for different things make sure to go. The hotel made it extremely easy to sign up for helicopter tours, luaus, bike rides down the volcano and numerous other activites. I highly recommend spending the first morning setting all of it up. They can sign you up for activites on other islands as well.The hotel is located right across from the International Marketplace which is a great spot to do some shopping. There's also a little bar/restaurant in there called Coconut Willie's which has some great bands to check out.All in all, I loved the Outrigger but Waikiki in general was a bit too crowded. If you're going to Hawaii make sure to visit more than just Oahu. You'll be missing out if you don't.

<Author>Netters
<Content>Great Stay Just returned from a great stay at Outrigger Waikiki on the Beach. We went to relax and that's what we did. I read many of reviews before booking this hotel and I'm glad that I did. When booking....(all hotels in Waikiki ) be sure to ask about construction. There is a lot and many hotels will not let you know unless you ask. The Outrigger was in the perfect spot and no construction. We rented the deluxe beach package every morning at 8:00am at the beach rental cabana. This costs $40.00 and includes two lounge chairs and an umbrella from 8:00 to 5:00pm. You can come and go all day. We were right on the ocean in the front row and it was well worth the money for the reserved space and location. We ate at Dukes, Chuck's Steakhouse, and the Hula Grill. Dukes bar was fun and the food was good. Chuck's was fairly average for the price. Hula Grill was incredible. It has great island decor and a limited menu but terrific food. Be sure to order the crab won tons and the shrimp scampi...they are excellent. There is also a small hidden deli to the far back left of the pool. It is down the walk and near the laundry. Great sandwiches for $5.00-$6.00. We found this and grabbed lunch at the hidden deli and ate on the beach. The food was great and we saved money so we could go for a nice dinner. We really loved the Outrigger. Excellent service and great location. I highly recommend this hotel!!!

<Author>joan1
<Content>Perfect choice! Well, after reading many reviews on this site( and others) we decided to stay at the Outrigger on the Beach, from Nov. 24- Dec2. We wanted beach front, good location, nice clean rooms , restaurant choices and a nice view. All that for less then 200 dollars a night. We got it at the Outrigger on the Beach. We paid 198. and got breakfast thrown in also. Great deal, the breakfast buffet was definately excellant, made on the spot omelettes, fresh fruit, yogurts, granola, fresh baked goods, french toast( very good) waffles with warm strawberry syrup( filled with strawberries!) bacon, sausages( two kinds) eggs, eggs benedicts, etc, etc, . We had breakfast there 7 days in a row and never got bored!We had room 1220, which we loved, not ocean front, but full ocean view, it was clean, had two double beds, and a sofa, plus a desk and a decent sized bathroom( only a half tub though, but we never use the tub on vacation, just shower) Mini fridge, iron and board, hair dryer, and safe (free) all in room also. Lots of closet space. We recomment staying on a higher floor just to avoid any noise , we think anthing about 8 or 9 would be fine. We requested and got, a room facing Diamond head, thank goodness as the rooms on the other side get awful noise from a roof fan on the Cheescake Factory. We could leave our door open at night and hear the waves crashing! Dukes which is the restaurant/ bar downstairs is great. Best price out of all the beach bars  for evening cocktails ( we checked, $9 for a Mai Tai at the Pink Palace, $8 at Sheraton, and 8 at Shorebird. )Food is good too!Dinner at Dukes has best salad bar around, we ate at the Shorebird ( at the Outrigger Reef) one night and were highly dissappointed! Highly recommend the Shrimp Scampi( tons of HUGE shrimps)  Staff at hotel were very pleasant, maid was effiecent, but, if you are the type who wants your sheets changed daily , you have to request that, there is a card you leave on your pillow that indicates that. Extra towels no problem! Pool is small and salt water, but, has the best location on the beach for lounging, get there EARLY and reserve a lounge on the top deck overlooking the beach, it is heaven! Ice water provied, bar service after 12( food also) and as many fresh towels as you want all day! Only negatives about stay were in regards to Waikiki in general, it is crowded, but, for us that energy is fun, some might not like it. I do recommend this location for number one convienence to everything, and after checking prices for all the other beach fronts the Outrigger on the Beach is the least exspensive for a WATERVIEW room( not a construction site room deal like some other hotels may offer you!) We found elevators to be quick enough, and have no idea what some posters though about the waits for them, we never encoutered more then a few minutes, which is normal we think .

<Author>LesJB47
<Content>Best location on Waikiki!!! We spent the second week of our honeymoon at the Outrigger Waikiki. Check in was easy, we arrived a little early, so they took our baggage and we stopped at Dukes for lunch. We had a partial ocean view room on the Cheesecake factory side of the hotel. We did hear the exhaust fan when we were on our deck, but it wasn't annoying. The sunsets were very nice from our balcony. Beds were comfy, bathroom very nice, room was made up prompty each day. The room had free ethernet with cables in the desk and free long distance within the US. The elevators did take awhile at times, but overall, didn't hold us up much.We got coffees at the Seattle Coffee company in the lower lobby, if you get the Big Kahuna package, you can use your 5 dollar vouchers there and essentially get a light breakfast for free each day. We had lunch at Dukes twice, which was reasonable and very good, you could also order for a smaller menu poolside. There was a small deli (Pai) near the pool which was extremely well priced and the sandwiches were a perfect light lunch. Drinks were great at Dukes and the Hawaiian beers were excellent, especially Kona Big Wave. We mixed it up between the beach and the pool. Definitely hit the beach early and rent lounge chairs and an umbrella. Never had a problem getting seats by the pool. It is not a quiet beach/pool experience, so don't expect it. It was a mixed group of people, friends traveling, honeymooners, and families. Bar service at the pool was excellent...and yes, bring your ID, but once the girls get to know you, you don't need it. Outrigger Waikiki is definitely in the hub of Waikiki, it is walking distance to great shopping and great restaurants. We mostly relaxed, since we had an action packed week before in Maui, but we thought Pearl Harbor and Diamond Head were well worth it. We also checked out the Magic of Polynesia across the street, fun, but not essential, and a little costly. The revolving restaurant across the street was a fun stop for a nightcap. All in all the Outrigger Waikiki was a great choice. We'd definitely come back!

<Author>rach_g
<Content>Great place to stay on Waikiki beach I just got back from a trip to America which included a 9 night stay in Waikiki. I highly recommend staying in the Outrigger on the Beach for anyone planning a stay on Waikiki beach. When we arrived, myself and my boyfriend were given a room on the cheesecake factory side of the hotel. We had read the reviews on this site before leaving and asked to move to the other side of the hotel. However, we were told by reception that we were high enough up to be away from any noise. However, when we got to the room and opened the balcony door, the noise of the fans was so loud. My boyfriend called reception and asked to be moved, they told us they'd move us the next day. Right enough, next day we were able to leave our cases in the room and head out for the morning and when we got back we (and our cases) had been moved to the other side of the hotel and had been given an upgraded room. The room and bathroom were large and spotlessly clean and came well equipped with iron, safe, hair dryer, fridge (not mini bar) and a big comfy bed!The staff were all really friendly and in the lower lobby the information desk would hand out small maps and direct you to almost anywhere.The pool was small but to be honest I didn't step near it because the beach is literally five steps from the back of the hotel. We got quite a warm spell for October and the beach was very busy most days so if you're looking for long uninhabited beaches then Waikiki is not the place for you. Best tip is get up early and rent a sun lounger and parasol.There are a few restaurants in the hotel itself however I only went to Dukes. The food there was good and reasonably inexpensive. You can either eat in the restaurant or in the bar area which has more of a snack menu.A previous poster mentioned ''only one drink per person'' this may come across as slightly misleading. The bar people would only let you have one drink at a time. If you wanted a drink then you had to be at the bar or at the table when the waiter/ess was taking the order and your own glass had to be half empty. I didn't see this as a huge problem and in some ways found it reassuring as it meant there was some control over alcohol consumption! One tip would be to bring ID at all times. My boyfriend and I are both in our mid - late twenties and were ID'edfor alcohol and cigarettes the whole time and this appeared to be the norm for anyone under 40. On our last day, the earthquake hit and the whole of waikiki lost power for nearly 12 hours. I must say, the hotel staff really handled it well. We got breakfast, lunch and dinner buffets on the house and the staff remained upbeat and helpful during such a rare occurance. One last tip - rent a car and take a drive to the north shore for a day!

As we ascended the elevator I noticed only the horribly ugly rugs that cover the lobby area and, again, hoards of people in line for one of the Outrigger's three restaurants. Our rooms were ocean view on the 3rd floor. My parents room had an obstructed view and was very small. Our room was bigger and had a full ocean view (we paid the same rate). We thought we were the lucky ones until we opened our sliding glass doors to hear the noise from Duke's Waikiki right below our balcony. It was loud out there until well after midnight and, after that, the noise moved to the hotel hallways. In the end, it was not horrible and it was not wonderful, it was just simply fine and disappointing given some of the other hotels we saw on the strip. The place had an overall feeling of Spring Break or Girls Gone Wild. Duke's was a madhouse most of the day and we fell asleep each night to some bad Jimmy Buffet song streaming up through our room as the backdrop to drunk people laughing and carrying on. Now, I am not against a good time but when a hotel bar will only give you one drink per person and you are traveling with people in their 40s and 60s, this has got to be a sign. If you want a relaxing stay (tough for Waikiki) at a beautiful hotel, travel further down the beach and spring for the Halekulani!

They didn't have a good time.This hotel is not a good idea if you have kids, especially if you have some that wake up during the night. But overall, it's in a great location near shopping, the Waikiki Beach and across from the International Marketplace. My only complaints are the thin walls and it can be very noisy even with all the doors closed... If you like the action, stay here, as long as you don't mind the noise and thin walls. <Content>Wonderful Stay in Waikiki We just returned from our trip to Oahu, Hawaii (July 13-19 2006)... stayed at the Outrigger Waikiki on the Beach. The beach is relatively small compared to other beaches on the island but the advantage of being in Waikiki and the location was great. The hotel room we had was a partial view; the room is fairly large and has a good size bathroom. We went to Lanikai Beach which is on the eastern shore of Oahu and that is a sight to see. This beach was rated the 2nd most beautiful beach in the world. There was no crowds and a wide shoreline....do take a trip to see it. The eastern coast of Oahu is simply very beautiful....we did all the tourist things like Pearl Harbor, Dole Plantation, Hananuno Bay and Diamond Head. There are two nice restaurants in the hotel; the food is good but need to make reservations a day in advance. There is lots of shopping along Kalakaua Avenue, especially if you like designer shops. The weather was wonderful and warm with no humidity. It was nice visiting Oahu...visited Maui and the Big Island 5 years ago. Of all the islands, Maui is the prettiest and has most dramatic landscape.

At the hotel both Dukes and the Hula grill provided excellent breakfasts and lunches at a reasonable cost for Hawaii. <Author>Birki
<Content>Our Best Vacation It was our first trip to Hawaii, recommended by my daughter and son-in-law who spent their honeymoon in Honolulu. They did not stay right on Waikiki Beach and wished they had, so...we booked 2 rooms at the Outrigger Waikiki Beach Hotel, a hotel where they had spent much time eatting and basking in the sun. We were not disappointed! My husband and I, along with my daughter, son-in-law and son, arrived June 30th for an 8-night stay. Upon our arrival, a friendly staff member checking us in noticed that our 2 rooms were not booked by our travel agent on the same floor. Although the hotel was booked, she was able to find 2 rooms on the 12th floor and upgraded us to partial ocean view rooms from city view rooms. The rooms were very nicely appointed with beautiful views...we were very comfortable. I had read in TripAdvisor about the loud fan on top of the Cheesecake Factory, so when I caught sight of that dreaded fan out the door to the lanai, I was worried that sleeping might prove difficult, however, that was not the case. We slept with the doors to the lanai closed and the room fan on, and our sleep was not disturbed.Although the hotel was almost totally booked, we never felt over-crowded anywhere in the hotel...well, maybe the elevators, but I felt that was reasonable in a hotel of its size. We were almost always seated fairly promptly at all of the restaurants. Each morning we had breakfast at the Hula Grill and always sat outside by the railing, overlooking the beach. The views were very pretty from our vantage point and the food was very good. The pancakes, french toast and omelets rivalled any I have ever eaten! We also enjoyed an evening dinner at the Hula Grill, dinners at Chuck's and of course, and lunches and dinners at Duke's Canoe Club. We found the food at all the hotel's restaurants to be very good and a good value (when compared to other restaurants in the Honolulu area). Every night we would walk the streets, looking for a new place to eat, but we seemed to always end up back at the hotel! We came to depend on the good food quality and the lively atmosphere (especially at Duke's). We only had one bad experience...we put our names in at Chuck's one evening and because the bar area was crowded, we left the restaurant and ordered drinks at the lobby bar at the Hula Grill. This bar is just outside of Chuck's...a mere 25 feet away. Shortly after we ordered the drinks, our table at Chuck's was ready. As we entered the restaurant, we were rudely told by the bartender and the young lady going to seat us that we'd have to leave the restaurant and finish our drinks outside before we'd be seated. I was offended that night Monday, July 3rd, perhaps because of the rude way we were informed. I, personally, did not order a drink that night at Chuck's (my personal revolt) and we did not return to that restaurant again even though the Shrimp Scampi were excellent. Other than that incident, we were always pleased with the staff at the restaurants, especially Bitna (B.B.) at the Hula Grill. She was fun and very efficient.We also enjoyed the pool area. Though the pool was not huge, it was never packed with people and pool chairs could always be found. It was very nice to have waitstaff from Duke's poolside so a drink and/or afternoon snack could be ordered. We enjoyed the pina coladas and chicken nachos while relaxing at the pool or on the lower pool deck. One very wonderful young man at the towel desk offered frozen washcloths on hot afternoons! That was a first for me!!I would recommend the Outrigger Waikiki Beach Hotel to any traveler who wants a fun, lively atmosphere yet classy and efficient hotel directly on the beach. It is in a perfect location of fine shops and restaurants. Friendly staff at the front desks and concierge desk were always helpful and offered tips to make our vacation such a success. I wish Hawaii wasn't so far away (at least from Wisconsin) so we could return again and again. I would definitely return to the Outrigger Waikiki Beach Hotel when we do return to Hawaii some day. I hope that day is soon.

The International Market is right across the street along with Macy's a whole bunch of designer stores and a lot of other stores. Lots of Restaurant too! You don't need a car but we did rent one. We used it almost everydate. Parking is expensive $18/day. The hotel staff is very friendly and always willing to help. My only negative comment would be the noise you can hear outside of your room. They need doors that are soundproof. Other reviews had indicated noise heard from the walls but that's not what I experienced. Couldn't hear anyone from the adjoining rooms. Only heard noise from the hallway. Room was fine. We were four in total and were fine with just one room. The room had two double beds and a pullout sofa. Our City view room had a partial view of the ocean. I wouldn't pay for ocean view. If that's what you want just go to the deck or the beach. Note: if you can get a room from the 14th floor and above it's the way to go. Floors 14 and above have a separate elevator. You won't have to deal with the issues other reviewers have mentioned (waiting a long time for an elevatior). For security purposes the elevators do not stop on the lower level after 10 pm. Security roams the floors too. I would definitely stay there again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>We highly recommend the Outrigger on the Beach! My husband and I stayed in an oceanfront room at the Outrigger on the Beach for 10 days for our 30th wedding anniversary last December - finally decided to write this review. We absolutely loved it! We had never been to Hawaii before. My husband really did his homework and studied up on several hotels, places to see, and things to do. We are so glad we chose the Outrigger. Everyone was courteous and friendly. The only drawback was, as others have said, the timeshare people in the lobby. We got so we didn't make eye contact with them. They were annoying. The rest of the hotel staff were very friendly.We highly recommend the book Oahu Revealed. It gives all the tips on places to go, and exactly how to get there. We rented a car, and went where we wanted when we wanted. We toured in the mornings, and relaxed on the beach back at the hotel in the afternoons. We climbed Diamond Head, and went to Pearl Harbor and the Missouri. Very near Pearl Harbor at the football stadium is a huge swap-meet. We also went to Hanauma Bay, then drove along Highway 72. What a view! We went to Sandy Beach, then to the North Shore to see the waves and surfers. Our very favorite place in all of Oahu was Lanikai Beach. It is the most beautiful beach - bluest water, and whitest sand - that we saw. You have to park on a side street and walk down a path to get there. It is not accessible to the tour buses, so is not at all crowded. It was absolutely gorgeous! We also stopped at Kualoa Park and saw Chinaman's Hat Island. We rode the Atlantis Submarine and saw stingrays, sea turtles, and all kinds of colorful fish. The day before we came home, we visited a rainforest.We had our complimentary breakfast at Duke's each morning. The selection there is so bountiful - and delicious. You must try a piece of Hula Pie from Duke's too. A few nights we ordered take-out either from Duke's or the Hula Grill and ate on our lanai. The smoothies at the coffee shop downstairs are very refreshing. We had dinner at Chuck's Steakhouse - delicious! The deli in the lobby is great for lunch!We HIGHLY recommend the Outrigger on the Beach.

<Author>hvtxmom
<Content>Great vacation! We just returned from Oahu and had a great time at the Outrigger. We stayed 2 nights in a City View room and loved every minute. We also stayed at the Ko Olina Beach Club for the next 2 nights, as my husband loves the city and I love peace and quiet, so we arranged for both. I was pleasantly surprised by how much I enjoyed the Outrigger and Waikiki.The hotel is tastefully decorated in Hawaiin themes, clean, and has the Aloha spirit. Even though our room was a City View, we still had a nice view of the ocean. We requested a room on the opposite side of the Cheesecake Factory and didn't hear any fan noise, although the street noise can be a little loud at times. The beds were comfortable and the bathrooms had everything including large granite countertops, make up mirrors, free safe, frig, and wonderful shampoos. Wish I could buy more of those! The room also had free internet access. We ate at Dukes most of the time and loved everything...service, food, and especially the Lava Flows. Put your name on the dinner waiting list on your way up from the pool at the end of the day and they will call your room when your table is ready. Nice touch! We ventured out to the International Market one day for lunch, but found the food court was a little shabby. I did have a great BBQ stick, though, and the Asian tourists seemed to love the food selections. We also picked up Cheesecake Factory deserts one night and ate them on our balcony...very nice!The pool felt a little small and crowded to me, but my husband loved it. We took a catamaran sail our last night for $15 each and had a great time. There are several choices for sailing in front of the Outrigger and we took the blue and white boat because they had a little dog on it's crew. The yellow one was packed with 20 somethings every night, due to free drinks. It was $5 more and seemed pretty roudy. The last sunset cruises that leave around 5:30pm go up $5, so we took the 4:00 one and had just as much fun. There were surfers everywhere and my favorite time was spent on the beach at sunset watching everyone come and go. The waves came in strong on the beach all day and were great for body surfing. We took morning trips to Pearl Harbor and Hanauma Bay and the valets were VERY helpful in giving us great directions. Again, I was very surprised at how much I loved being in the heart of the action on Waikiki. The Ko Olina was beautiful and peaceful, but we both found outselves getting a little bored by the second day. We had a great trip, but our best memories were surprisingly at the Outrigger. Oloha!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Vegas on the Beach If you're in your 20s and love to party or your a bigtime shopper who loves to spend spend spend; you'll love Waikiki. Families or plus 40 couples or friends will be less inspired. That's not to say the Outrigger isn't a really great hotel. It is and its located right in the heart of Waikiki/ The rooms are clean, the bathrooms feature limestone-marble-like tile surfaces and modern fixtures, the sound proofing is pretty darn good鈥攗nless you leave your sliding door open to hear the surf (which you can hear even in the 11th floor rooms). The beach tends to throb late into the night, so if you're trying to stay on PST or MST (which means hitting the bed at 8Pm and getting up at 4:30AM) you'll have to wear earplugs. The housekeeping staff is really great about helping out. The Hula Grill offers excellent breakfasts, great beachside views and fairly decent prices for a hotel on the beach! The prices at Duke's, below on the beach, are pretty expensive for what you get. (side bar: Foods pretty good but about what you expect. In fact,most of the food in Honolulu at the restaurants is just so-so. Stay out of the Chinese restaurants. They're wretched. I hit three before I swore them off. Japanese is the way to go). Also, be sure to checkout the historical/art exhibits near the Outrigger canoe in the OW's lobby! It offer priceless insight into Hawaiian culture. The swimming pool features sparkling clear salt water instead of chlorine. A huge plus. You can use your room card to get towels down there. But you probably won't use it if you came for the ocean....If you're tempted to take any of the gazillion catamaran cruises available on the beach out for snorkeling, forgettaboutit. They're a joke. They take you out about 300 yards, shamelessly chum for fish with cookies, and drop you in the middle of it all. Sure you see a few fish but you also fight currents and waves and the number of fish is about three species total, and maybe a turtle or two (swimming away from you as quickly as possible). Then afterwards they take you out into the ocean for a hour long out and back cruise to nowhere. It's a yawner, unless you were really dying to see the cityscape views of Honolulu. The Outrigger's new Plantation Spa is fantastic...just opened on the top floor; the prices are reasonable, the therapists highly skilled and the serene atmosphere is amazing with ocean views straight out to the horizon. I'd love to sit out in the rooftop hottubs in thevening! The very large couples massage room is extraordinary for the spa world, and the treatments and atmosphere will blow you away. The changing rooms feature a modern Hawaiian aesthethic.This is a spa treat worth considering if you plan to stay at the OW. Be sure to ask for a room near the express elevator so you can walk out of your room and take a direct lift to the spa (which is also next to a really great exercise room with all the modern cardio equipment).The biggest drawback to staying at the OW, and its true for many of the hotels on this strip, is that you pay a premium for parking. $18 a day plus tips. Even if you have a fly-car-stay package. Better idea: Take Speedy Shuttle from the airport and use the downtown shuttles to get around to Pearl Harbor or even around the island. For $2 per stop you can go all the way to Halaweia and Kanehoe or Hanauma Bay and back to Waikiki.

<Author>kozmo13
<Content>Great Stay ay Outrigger Waikiki on the Beach This is an excellent hotel. I'd dare to say the best you'll find in Waikiki. This isn't because it is a great facility, but rather its absolute prime location. It is directly across the street from the International Marketplace, a truly fascinating part of Hawaii and for sure a great souvenir stop. It鈥檚 within walking distance to the zoo, surfing, and almost the entire strip.HIGH POINTS: This hotel has a friendly and helpful staff that will seek to engage you. I find this far different from many other shops, restaurants, and hotels you are likely to encounter in Hawaii. For example, each day my wife and two small children set out to explore locations on the East and North shores. The valets would see to it that we had accurate direction in hand no matter how long it took. (At no point did they push for a tip or could they assume they were getting one- but of course they did). Housekeeping frequently made it a point to engage us to find out if there was anything else we needed. Our room, although small, was well appointed and very comfortable. It had a very nice bathroom and (empty) refrigerator. Free in-room internet and WIFI in the lobby and pool area. But, there is nowhere to sit!!LOW POINTS: Check in can be abrupt. They do seem a little too serious for the setting. The overall facility is much smaller than their website would make it seem. There is one relatively small pool and a small hot tub. There are no kiddy pools or even a shallow end. The total square footage devoted to outdoor activity (aside from public beach) is far too small to support the number of rooms and guests, but they do make it seem less crowded through an intelligent multi-level design.FOOD: The hotel has at least 2 (I think more) excellent restaurants. We ate many times at Duke鈥檚 and found it to be excellent food and an unbelievable bargain compared to other food in the area. For example; on Mother鈥檚 day, all 4 of us ate at their Sunday brunch for $35 with a nice tip. The food was some of the best I had on a 3 week trip to various islands in Hawaii. When compared to the $20 we spent eating a Waikiki fast-food breakfast on the way to the Zoo (also close), it truly seems like a bargain. The only major issue is the lack of sit down restaurants in the direct vicinity of the hotel. The only one was Cheesecake factory which had a perpetual 80-90 minute wait (total waste of time). In the end, we opted to eat at the most multi-cultural food court probably one of the best the planet many nights, the food court of the International market. It was great and a 2 minute walk. There was everything from cold coconuts, to sushi, hamburgers, Korean BBQ, pizza, Mexican, local cuisine鈥?all excellent and frequently accompanied by a free show.Overall, I鈥檇 say this is an excellent selection for Oahu and Waikiki. The only caveat is that one should dig deep for the best price. After getting the 鈥渁bsolute best price鈥?from a website that advertises that they beat everyone by 20%, I found the exact room for $300 less for 4 nights on the very next site I visited. Of course the first website did try hard to convince me that their special price was sold out (unless I booked a package) despite the fact that literally every other site (including the hotel) said it wasn鈥檛. Interestingly, they were still advertising their 鈥渟old out鈥?rate weeks after telling me it wasn鈥檛 available. So, be aware鈥?most prices in Oahu are a moving target.Have fun (and learn to surf)!!

<Author>ellbelle
<Content>Great location Just returned from a week long stay at the OW. This was our third time (in 16 years), but our 10 year olds first time. We chose the OW due to the location, especially that it is across from the IMP and for my shopaholic daughter this was a good fit. We did request our city view room to be on the opposite side of the Cheesecake Factory, this was not an unusual request according the the front desk. We then checked back at 1pm, and a room was ready.The room was a great size for three, with plenty of drawer space, and an ample closet for hang up clothes and luggage. The toilet and shower (no bathtub, although there are rooms that have them) is in a closet sized area, just as another reviewer has said. A bit cramped, but just keep the sliding door open. The lanai is tight with a table and two chairs, but a third chair can be pulled up from the inside (leave the door open) for all to enjoy. Our room was the second from the end, but we had a great view of the water, much better than I remember. The pool is small with no shade, but I knew this already. I did not run down in the early morning to reserve a chaise, but I had no trouble finding one or two chaises together in the afternoon (2ish). One afternnon I did notice that there were chaises that looked like they had not been used all day. There should be a time limit on unused chaises.For beach time, renting an umbrella and chaises is the way to go. The fee for this was $40.00 but I felt it was worth it. Just get down to beach by 7:45, and they will get it set up for you. This is yours for the day, so feel free to come an go as you choose. Be sure to have your umbrella set up away from the water, that way when the tide comes in, you are safe. We saw many in the first row get run out of their area, because all their things were getting wet. There is a great choice of restaurants, Duke's is always busy, but they will give you a pager. Having Seattle's Best Coffee in the lobby, is a nice supplement to the inroom coffee, and not expensive.For location, the OW can't be beat. It is a very busy hotel, with people everywhere. The beach is a good swimming beach but wall to wall people. It's a bit distracting to attempt to read, but great for people watching. Had I realized that we would do as much pool and beach time, I would have selected the HHV, but I am not disapointed choosing OW again.

<Author>reed13ja
<Content>Best Location on the Beach! My husband and I traveled to Honolulu on April 4-11 of 2006. We stayed at the Outrigger Waikiki on the Beach. There are many other hotels in the Outrigger/Ohana chain in Waikiki, and they have similar names so be careful when reading reviews. This hotel is the flagship of the chain, and it is right on the beach in Waikiki. While walking the beach, we explored many other hotels and we agree that this hotel has the absolute best beach location for swimming and relaxing on the sand. The water in front of the hotel is not blocked by manmade concrete walls, as is it in front of many other hotels. The bottom of the ocean is mostly sandy with only a few hard corals and rocks, due to a natrual spring that originally emptied into the ocean right under where the hotel was built. The waves are gentle enough for small children to swim, and the water was shallow enough for me to stand on the bottom about 50 yards out. (I am about 5'10) There are plenty of activities close by, including catamaran and canoe rides, surf board and boogie board rentals. Down the beach to the left past the next hotel is a public beach area which is popular for surfing lessons. The waves here are a bit larger and the view from the Outrigger of the surfers and the famous Diamondhead beyond is great. The hotel has a decent pool and gym area, nothing phenomenal though. The hot tub was often crowded with kids and closes down at 3PM on Friday, Saturday, and Sundays to make room for live entertainment. There are plenty of beach chairs available for free on the pool decks, and for rent on the beach (umbrellas as well). The rental prices were a bit steep, $20 for a umbrella and $15 for a chaise lounge for the day. I would recommend going to one of the neighboring tourist shops and buying your own if you plan on spending a lot of time on the beach.As for the hotel itself, the resteraunts were great. The famous Duke's lives up to its reputation with great views and delicious food. In fact, one morning we had breakfast there we saw a tour group from Maui that was doing a one day tour of Oahu and made Duke's one of their stops. The hotel has a tour and activities desk with reasonably priced tours and rental cars. You could get them cheaper out on the street, but you typically have to be subjected to some kind of timeshare presentation.The room was great, very nicely decorated and well kept. You can tell the hotel has been recently renovated. The only complaint I have is noise from the hallways and adjoining doors to the rooms next door. A few times I had trouble getting to sleep because I could hear conversations in the hall as if the people were right next to the bed. I would recommend requesting a room away from the elevators. As for the views, we booked a city view room and ended up in the second to last room in the hallway. The hotel is situated perpendicular to the beach, so that rooms on the beach have a full on frontal view of the water, but the majority of rooms are along the sides of the hotel, with views of the surronding city. However, when we stepped out onto our balcony, we had a beautiful view of the beach and ocean. If you are interested in seeing the water, but not paying the full price of the ocean view, I would recommend the city view room. I believe they determine their pricing based on the view from the bed inside the room, not from the balcony. I would guess that every room in the hotel above the 4th floor would have a good view of the beach from the balcony.The International Market Place, a great place to get souveniers was right across the street. It is a very interesting open-air market covered by trees. You have to see it to believe it. There is a lot of construction going on along the street behind the hotel. They are improving the beach walk and adding a ton of great restaraunts and shopping. However, the construction noise is far enough away that you never hear it on the beach, and it didnt bother me even when we napped in the middle of the day in our room. It was not right on top of the Outrigger, but I assume it would be a little more bothersome at some of the hotels closer to the work.All in all, the Outrigger was a great hotel. We got a bargain, paying just under $150 a night to stay here. But with the great location, amenities, and service, I would have still considered paying upwards of $250 a night to be a bargain.

Maybe I didn't have the right look, or maybe my new york accent was the thing that did it or maybe the staff who is suppose to treat all people the same, choose not to uphold the Hawaiian tradition we have heard so much about...Mahola.

<Author>Temeha
<Content>Mixed Feelings about the OWB Now that many guests are giving the OWB glowing reviews, it seesm that I'm going to throw a spanner in the works. We just returned from a 10 day stay at the Outrigger Waikiki, and this is going to be a hard one because we felt there are good points and not so good points about the hotel. First the good - the hotel is in a great location, being right on the beach, directly across the street from the International Market Place, and surrounded by many shops and dining options. Plus it is a quick stroll to Kuhio Ave, which is where all the major bus stops are in Waikiki. This close proximity to many attractions makes it a great option for those who do not wish to hire a car and would rather be within walking distance to a lot of things. The rooms seem to have been recently refurbished and they are a good size with comfortable beds and reasonably attractive decor. Our very small balcony overlooked a neighbouring shopping complex with a huge exhaust fan that was extremely noisy when the door was open. However, thankfully when the door was closed the noise was minimised significantly. The rest of the view was rather nice, particularly at night. Ok, now time for the big complaints....being a large hotel, it was EXTREMELY busy and noisy, so if you're looking for a nice, quiet, relaxing  hassle-free holiday, this is not the place for you. This is exactly the type of holiday we were looking for, and frankly we left feeling just as stressed as we were when we arrived. NOISE: the overall level of noise in and around the hotel was unacceptable. We discovered we were in an interconnecting room and the guests in the other room were a mother and her 2 extremely naughty children. One night around 10:30pm the yelling, swearing and fighting got so bad I was so close to calling security. Afraid of the consequences, I decided to butt out and hope it stopped soon! But I can assure you, I heard every word, slap and scream as plain as if they were in the very same room as us. The walls are definitely paper thin, and you can hear voices, thuds, showers running and toilets flushing all day and night. And having children in the room next door meant we rarely enjoyed a nice sleep-in because they were up yelling and screaming at each other at day break. Also you can hear telephones ringing from other rooms. Certainly not what you need to hear on holidays. ELEVATORS: were so full, and would just about stop on every floor on the way down, so patience is required. The only time they weren't full was early in the mornings. BARS/DINING: We dined at the Hula Grill a couple of times and found the food  service of excellent quality. However, you must get there early (around 5-6pm) if you dont want to wait for a table. Even when we made reservations we found ourselves waiting in the over-crowded bar with a pager. So dont bother making reservations, just turn up and be prepared to wait. The Plantation Bar was great for a happy hour drink, and very quiet and relaxing around 4-5pm, but be prepared for the evening rush by around 6pm. We didn't even bother trying to sit and drink and Dukes because it was always so full/overcrowded and extremely noisy. It was impossible to sit and have a nice conversation because of the deafening noise. The line for dinner every night was just unbelievable, so again we only ate there once and that was at 5pm because any time after 6 you usually have to wait at least an hour or two for a table. If you are not too hungry get there early and work up an appetite while you wait in line. POOL/BEACH - this is my biggest gripe by far. They have a ridiculous and (I think) extremely rude system whereby guests are able to reserve the sun lounges by the pool all day long, whether they use them or not. Unless you got to the to pool at 7am and reserved a chair, it was very difficult to get one unless you stood there and stalked like a vulture until someone finally left or removed their towel (being the reserved sign). I saw many chairs reserved and never used all day long! I found this extremely inconsiderate and rude to other guests. If you're not swimming in the pool/beach or close by then as far as I'm concerned you shouldn't be able to reserve your chair for the rest of the day. So out of 10 days we got to sit by the pool twice. I wasn't happy at all. The beach directly in front is also very crowded and its hard to get a nice piece of sand. However, if you enjoy the whole crowd scene then this might be just the place for you. Staff were always friendly and welcoming, and service was fairly efficient, but overall its a very busy, hectic, noisy and happening place, so if you enjoy the peace and quiet and being able to relax while on holidays, I wouldn't recommend this hotel at all. I doubt we will return to Oahu because we felt the whole island was overcrowded and overrated, but if by chance we do I would definitely opt for something smaller and more intimite next time.

My husband had written to the GM of the property prior to us leaving advising of my birthday. Each day a newsletter announcing birthdays, anniversarys etc was delivered to each room. My birthday was not acknowledged so either he did not receive the letter or didn't care. Disappointing.If you were to stay at this Outrigger I would suggest that if you like to be asleep before midnight EVERY night you should NOT splash out for an Ocean Front Room. The music and noise levels emanating from Dukes below is extremely loud and sleep impossible even with the doors and curtains shut. Save your money and go for a Part Ocean view - your stress levels will be contained. Friday Saturday and Sunday nights are the worst as live bands start at 3pm...and some of them are not actually all that great! We spent alot of time across the street at the Sheraton Princess Kailani and back at our old favourite the Outrigger Reef - they have live Hawaiian Music each night - it was peaceful and conveyed the ALOHA spirit far more than anything we heard at Dukes in 12 days.And now to the pool. This is not a large pool and poolside chairs are at a premium. I suspect there is a system at the pool for guests who return year after year ( perhaps timeshare?) The pool staff have a printout each day and appear to 'reserve' chairs for anyone on this list but if you are not on the list don't expect any favours. After being disappointed several days in a row I asked how you go about getting a chair reserved and was told quite bluntly to come down at 6:30 am and put your towel down on a chair. So as you can imagine after being awake until midnight due to the racket below and having to get up at 6:30 am to reserve a chair this was not the relaxing holiday we had planned on. Even more disappointing was that a quarter of these 'reserved' lounges weren't used all day! Also the pool closed at 6pm each day and the hot tub at 3pm some days.The breakfast buffet at Dukes was very average - if it had not been included in our package we would not have gone there. The fruit was under ripe and the tea and coffee luke warm. Our one eveing meal at Dukes in the evening was ruined by a smart mouthed male waiter who over promised and under delivered.So to sum up this is not what I expected of Outriggers Flagship property. Next visit I will return to the Outrigger Reef where the staff have a true spirit of ALOHA, the atmosphere is welcoming and comfortable, the rooms though a little tired are spacious and quiet( though I believe they are being renovated as we speak )the entertainment is Hawaiian, the pool and hot tubs are opened late into the night and there are oodles of lounges, the restaurants are casual and well staffed and you are very sad to leave what had become your home away from home. We felt no attachment to the Outrigger Waikiki at all and this property could learn many valuable lessons from her sister property up the beach.

<Content>Great Honeymoon I was prepared to be unimpressed but couldn't have asked for more. The view in our room was the type of ocean view that one would want on Waikiki. Diamond Head to the left and prime beach view below and to the right. As far as the room..it was very nice and the service was supreme. We attempted to use the email service on the TV - I purchased it at 11:30 am and when we returned after lunch it no longer worked. Dukes Bar in the lobby was just great and besides the excellent breakfast we found ourselves returning for drinks, a burger at lunch, and dinner one night. I would highly recommend The Ocean House at Outrigger on the Reef though because they really went all out to make our dinner special...free dessert, a few drinks, and a picture taken at the table. Word of advice...if you are on your honeymoon...tell the hostess at ever place you go. We sat beachside at every restaurant we went to. We capped off the week at the Royal Hawaiian brunch which was just wonderful. Most fun on the trip was Snorkeling at Hanauma Bay, Hiking Diamond Head, Drinks at The Royal Hawaiian, Lava Cake at Roy's Restaurant (although $40 cab ride each way put a damper on what otherwise was an awesome meal), and a special mention of the Sunset Catamaran at Outrigger Reef...much better than Mai Tai Catamaran.......unlimited drinks..better ride and we saw dolphins. Check out Magnum Tours down from the hotel.....we spent hardly anything on our tours ($25 a piece for an all day island circle tour...$7 to Pearl harbor and the flea market, $8 to Hanauma Bay including rental of mask, fins, snorkel) and it all went off without a hitch......I say pass on any Luau though.....very lame....and take a small handgun to shoot any time share condo salesmen that circle like sharks all over the main strip. As everyone does we plan to return...one day and we will stay at Outrigger Waikiki again. It was our style. We enjoyed The Royal Hawaiian and Moana Surfrider bars and property but we both agreed that Outrigger was more what we needed and wanted.

<Author>cherbonsy
<Content>A 4 star hotel with 3 star allure Things could be worse at the Outrigger Waikiki on the Beach, but considering the price for this supposedly 4 star hotel, there wasn't a whole lot to get excited about. On the pros side, the rooms were large, and the location on Waikiki Beach is outstanding. Even the partial ocean view rooms have a decent peek of the Pacific, and there is surfboard, outrigger and catamaran rental on the beach right outside the hotel. Service at the front desk area is competent, and the valet service (while mandatory - no self parking - and rather pricey at $18/night) is quick and pleasant. The Hula Grill and Duke's restaurants both serve great food (and the prior will serve you a free ice-cream sandwich desert if you tell them you're a returning diner).On the cons side, the hotel, built in 1967, felt worn with the renovations being of sub-Ikea quality. The walls are really thin and if the couple next door are on honeymoon or have kids, you'll know. While broadband service is included with the price of the room, I averaged 5Kbps ... a lot slower than simple dial-up. Common to many of the hotels in Waikiki, the elevators were slow (expect up to 5 minutes wait time in the lobby), and customer service via the phone was unreliable (it took 3 calls to get the hotel to process a request for 3rd party billing my room).All in all, while competitive for Waikiki, the Outrigger Waikiki on the Beach is too pricey considering the drawbacks.

Pretty good and a good value at 12/person. Again, it's right on the beach so that's a plus.Great location for the hotel in general. In the middle of the Kalakau Ave with tons to do around there. If you rent a car, valet is $18 a day but the guys in front are plesant.Overall I would definitely stay here again, but would definintely either go big with an Ocean Front room or go cheap with a City room. The only thing that would make it better would be some kind of rewards program (thus I considered the Hyatt for that reason).

<Content>Simply the best!  We just got back from a 1-week stay at the Outrigger Waikiki on the Beach. When we arrived, we had no lines. When the sliding glass door to the balcony was opened, you could here the relaxing sound of waves crashing on the shore. Note: A/C turns off when sliding door is open to conserve energy. Don't sleep with door open if you like it cool. All the staff we encountered were very friendly. For a quick snack try the hotel snack shop (near the pool). They have a very unique hot dog made from hamburger. Work out center looks into bottom of swimming pool. A fun way to watch your kids when you work out. The hotel is located on one of the premier shopping and dining strips. Everything is a short walk away. The beach was nice but had some rock/coral in the water. Larger beach is a short walk away. Overall we were very satisfied. We had a great rate from Expedia and we would highly recommend this hotel.

<Author>riffsmom
<Content>Outrigger Waikiki -location,location, location The Outrigger Waikiki on the Beach is in a perfect location right in the center of Waikiki. The beach istself has a lovely sandy bottom and you can easily walk to anywhere. Check-in was done in a relaxed personal manner. If you want a view of the beach but want to pay city view prices ask for a room in the center. Rooms ending in 00and 01(400,500etc.)are on the eastern side of the hotel. There is some noise from the top of the Royal Hawaiian shopping center but to me it was white noise, kind of like an air conditioner and it didn't bother me. You can see out to the beach and across rooftops to the lights of the city. rooms ending with 12 and 14 (512,514 etc.) are on the west side. You can see the beach, there is less noise but you are hemmed in by the taller hotel (MoanaSurfrider) next door. We had a lovely meal at the Hula Grill. It overlooks the beach and is above Duke's so you can hear the entertainment but don't have to deal with the noisy crowd there. All the service people were polite and helpful. They have a good activities desk, outriggers and catamaran right there. The pool has shady spots. All in all I would say it was a fun place to stay.

<Author>azaccone
<Content>Ideal location on Waikiki Although my wife and I were a bit disappointed in being turned down for an upgrade as our 15th floor ocean view room was more of a City View (opposite Diamondhead), we highly recommended this facility. The bottle of champagne for our honeymoon was a nice touch and the overall appearance of the room was immaculate and well appointed. Our package included buffet breakfast at Dukes or a sit down breakfast at the Hula Grill which served ample breakfast fare even if one had to pay the $12.95 pp.I highly recommend the Hula Grill for happy hour as they have great drink and appetizer specials. My fave is the crab and mac nut wontons. I also recommend the Na Hoku catamaran cocktail cruise which is a two hour morning or sunset cruise off Waikiki which sets sail right on the hotel's beach. They are very generous with the alcohol (beer, rum, scotch, champagne etc.) and it attracts some real characters. For a nice but pricey meal out, I recommend Alan Wongs and their 7 course chef's choice menu. Back to the hotel... Although I am not one for lounge acts, I highly recommend the Society of Seven show. These guys are brilliant.I would however, eat elsewhere instead of wasting your money on the very average and rushed buffet. The room itself (70's retro) does not lend itself to a fine dining experience. The biggest turnoff however, are the pushy timeshare people on the lower level of the hotel. Do not make eye contact with them and do not be afraid of being rude by ignoring them. I recommend taking the escalator to and from the lobby level and avoid this area at all costs. Being from NY, I am used to pushy people but they are close contenders. Yes, the parking here is exorbitant. However, this is par for the course in Honolulu. The valets are very efficient and frequent tipping is highly recommended for even quicker service. Another great perk offered by Outrigger is the traditional Hawaiian vow renewal ceremony on the grounds of the Outrigger Reef. This is a complimentary service offered every Tuesday and Friday and made for a very memorable experience for us. Anyway, I can drone on about what a great place this is overall and how we will probably return, but I will let the previous reviews speak for themselves.

<Content>Not as great as I read.... We stayed at the Outrigger for our Honeymoon from October 29th through November 5th. We booked a standard City View in hopes of an upgrade after reading about the possibility of one on this site, but even though it was our Honeymoon, we were not upgraded. We were on the 4th floor (which is actually the 6th), and we heard a lot of street traffic as well. If sleep is in your plans in Hawaii, try a hotel with better construction. The other complaint I had was with Dukes. We thought we were going to have a fun bar to hang out at and every night we tried to go there, there was no seating available, it was hot and uncomfortable and too many people crammed into the small bar space. We hit every bar in Waikiki and Dukes was by far our least favorite (and we are young!) So, my review is neutral because the location is awesome, but noise is quite a problem (at least to us it was!). When we go back, we will not be staying at the Outrigger. Next door at the Royal Hawaiian seemed much better!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Look no further if you want to stay on the beach in Waikiki! Let me first say that I viewed TripAdvisor quite a bit before confirming my hotels and itinerary in Oahu (this website along with the book Oahu Revealed by Andrew Doughty and Harriett Friedman). I wanted to return the favor by posting my own review. My family (myself, wife and two kids - ages 8 and 2) just came back on Sunday the 16th from an incredible week-long vacation. The Outrigger on Waikiki Beach is fab... nothing but a good experience all the way around. From the moment we arrived, we knew we had made the right decision. It was between the Royal Hawaiian and Sheraton Moana Surfrider right on the water - and on the best part of the beach in my opinion. I didn't know quite what to expect as this was our first trip to Hawaii but this was, indeed, the place to stay. Due to an initial on-line reservation glitch, we were upgraded to an oceanview room. The view was great, the room was big and the bed comfortable. Dukes - a great place to eat (as I've been to the one in Malibu as I grew up just a few miles away) - is in the hotel as well as a convenience store and a Seattle's Best Coffee (perfect for coffee, bagels, muffins, etc. for breakfast). Everything was so convenient to the location of the hotel... walking distance to many great restaurants and shops. A first class operation all the way through - check-in, information desk, concierge and housekeeping. And the valet - Nelson - remembered my name the entire week. My highest recommendation to all looking for a great and reasonable hotel. As for activities, we went to Germaine's Luau our second night in town and it was cool... Our guide - Cousin Aka - simply rocked. An informative Hawaii native that really made all the difference... the food was okay but the entertainment (specifically the hula dancers) and the tour guide were memorable. I suggest you request Cousin Aka by name if you take the luau. He'll make your bus ride to the luau considerably seem shorter. We went to Pearl Harbor on Tuesday, the Byodo-In Temple (Valley of the Temples) and North Shore on Wednesday. Make sure you ring the ball at the Byodo-In Temple for good luck! Played golf at the toughest, yet most beautiful course, I've ever played (and I've been playing 28 years - about a ten handicap) on Thursday called Luana Hills... it's Jurassic Park with many blind holes that you can't see until your second and sometimes third shot. I shot 15 strokes over my handicap so bring a lot of golf balls! My dad, who's in excellent shape at the age of 75, was exhausted by the end of the day as they closed the fairways to carts (unbeknownst to us until we got there...). If you're looking for a memorable experience, this is the course. On that same day, my wife and two kids went to the Outrigger Reef and embarked on the Outrigger Catamaran that departs from the hotel. I took my kids and dad the following day... they couldn't get enough! This might be the best entertainment value in Hawaii - $40 total for two adults and one child (my two year old was free). Friday was our 10th Anniversary so we checked out of the Outrigger and checked in to the Kahala Mandarin Oriental. If you want to be out of the hustle-and-bustle of Waikiki, I highly recommend this hotel... probably the nicest we've ever stayed in anywhere. The service and landscape was absolutely spectacular! Another five star rating from me. You're greeted at the front desk by a cold towel offering. After you check-in, they personally bring you to your room and ask if it's up to all your expectations. The person who served us the moment we got in was Joy... not only extremely knowledgeable but probably one of the most attractive women on the Island! It was all good. The room, pool, grounds and service were all unbelievable. As they say, all it takes is money. But the splurge was worth every penny. Our eight year old daughter enjoyed Dolphin Quest at the hotel and both kids loved the manta rays and turtles swimming in the lagoons. One final recommendation is Alan Wongs restaurant (on S. King Street)... we heard it was one of the best restaurants in town and we ended up going there for our 10th anniversary celebration - Ginger Crusted Onaga followed by the Chocolate Sampler. All the waiters signed a menu wishing us Happy Anniversary. I can't think of a better restaurant in recent memory. Go to all the above and have the time of your lives like we did! We can't wait to return!  
<Date>Oct 19, 2005

<Content>Okay hotel - great location Booked solely due to location and reviews on this site. Paid about US $350 per night so I had high expectations for this hotel. Found the room to be slightly larger than normal and comfort wise it was really good. Found the staff not helpful and not very friendly which I didn't expect. We arrived at 9pm and got no help with our bags from the one bell hop - barely even bothered to tell us where to check in!! Asked very nicely for upgrade and was knocked back - 2 small children may have been the reason?? Were placed on west side of hotel which has a nice outlook, but is very loud due to airconditioning next door! Asked again for upgrade but were told it would be another US$110 per night! Duke's breakfast coupons were free, but only 2 per day and we were a party of 4. Breakfast was good, but not the best I've ever had. What saved this hotel for us was the fantastic location and just the magic of Waikiki. The kids loved the pool and the beach - we all did. Laundry facilities were good too - always a bonus with little kids. I would look elsewhere next time we visit Honolulu.

<Author>BL24
<Content>Great location My wife and I recently spent the second week of our honeymoon at the Outrigger on the Beach. We reserved a city view room, but upon check-in, we were upgraded to a partial ocean view room which was much larger. One problem though- our upgrade was on a smoking floor which they told us would be the case. We went with it though because the view (12th floor)and room were better and it didn't smell very smokey. On the second night, the room next door to us (we had an adjoining door) was very loud- they had a loud child and a hairdryer going at 12:45am and we could hear everything crystal clear. We asked to be moved to another room and went with the same sized room with a king bed to the 3rd floor but we were one room away from an actual ocean front room so the view was even better. Duke's is a can't miss for any meal and a drink and the atmosphere is great. The Hula Grill is also good and runs happy hour specials where I had delicious fish and chips for around $6.00! The elevators aren't that bad but my only issue is having to have your key ready all the time to enter your floor number and I found this to be a big inconveneince. Service in all aspects at this hotel was great from the housekeeping to front desk to the waitstaff at Duke's. And by the way- if you're staying at this Outrigger and want to eat at Duke's, all you have to do is call Duke's and they call you when a table is ready for dinner- no reservation needed! One of the perks for staying here.This hotel is right in the middle of everything and right on the beach so it's location is unbeatable. Take a circle island tour or just enjoy the pool and beach. Be sure to get a raft to float on in the ocean- such a relaxing time. I would definitely go back to the Outrigger Waikiki on the Beach.

<Author>RobertMilne
<Content>Great hotel, great location but rather noisy on the west side I have recently returned to Scotland from Hawaii having stayed at this hotel for 19 nights. The hotel has a great location facing directly onto Waikiki beach. The room was very spacious and very comfortable and the staff were very helpful with any queries I had. The only downside of our stay (and it is worth noting) is that if you are located anywhere on the west side of the hotel, you will find the persistent drone of the fans on the roof of the Royal Hawaiian shopping centre quite unbearable. I did ask if we could be moved to the east facing side after a few days staying there, but the only room available was on the first floor looking onto Kalakau Avenue so we decided to stay where we were. The noise from the fans does not allow you to relax on the balcony unless you have come prepared with earplugs - it can also be heard even when the balcony doors are closed. We did however have a good view of the beach and the valet parking staff were first class.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Breathtaking! We just returned from a 7 night stay at The Outrigger Waikiki for our 10th anniversary. I have to say that everything about this hotel was amazing. We were on the 14th floor. We had reserved an ocean front room since it was our anniversary trip. We never had a problem waiting on the elevator. We were told we could use the express elevator, but we didn't find it until our last day. There really was no need because there were three main elevators, and they moved pretty fast. Only problem is you have to insert your key to go over the 10th floor, I believe. There were some people putting their keys in to go to the first floor, but it wasn't necessary. There should be a little plaque or something so that people know when they have to fumble around and get their keys and when they don't need it. The view from the room was amazing! We had Diamond Head to the left and the beach right out front and to the right. The maid service was amazing. When we returned to the room in the evenings after walking the strip, our bed had already been turned down, there was candy and flowers on our pillows and our towels and soaps had already been restocked. The lotion and shampoo provided by the hotel smelled absolutely amazing. There is a Lei making class on Fridays and it was so much fun. The beach was crowded, but there is always room for a couple more people. We went every day except the day we went snorkeling at Hanauma Bay. Be sure to go ahead and take with you a float or purchase one for less than $5 in the lobby stores. The surf in front of the hotel is pefect for floating around and relaxing. We also bought a couple of beach mats for $1.25 each. They are cheaply made, but for that price, we didn't expect much. The sand on Waikiki is so soft, it feels like you are walking on butter when you are in the water. There were sea turtles swimmig along with us almost every day. This was our first trip to Hawaii and we were amazed around every corner. We rented a car for our entire stay and used it every single day. There is a $15 a day charge for parking, and the valet did not wait around for a tip, we did tip them some, but we didn't tip every day just because we couldn't afford it. We rode up the West coast Highway(H1-west maybe??) and stopped at every lookout and they were beautiful. We went up to Hwy 61 and took it back to the hotel. The next day we went up the Pali Hwy toward the North Shore and, again, breathtaking views. We went to the Luau at the Polynesian Cultural Center. The package we purchased included the tour of the island, the Luau and the nighttime fire show. Well worth every penny. This was, by far, the best experience we had in Hawaii. We visited the Dole Pineapple Plantation and it was more of an educational experience. It was pretty neat, but not worth the time we spent. If you have kids with you, then this would be great for them, because the only thing you have to pay for is the train ride and the kids would love that. The best place to buy souvenirs is at the ABC stores(every 100 feet or so) or the International Marketplace(bargain with the sellers). We will go back to Hawaii, and if we go back to Waikiki we will stay at the hotel. Next time, we plan to visit other island though, but we will look for the Outrigger name wherever we go.  
<Date>Sep 26, 2005
<Rating>5	3	5	-1	5	-1	5	-1
